tion of struts, but it is to be noted that the excavation is an on-going process: the excavations
proceeds as the struts are being installed. Moreover, the end date of each stage corresponds to
the start of the subsequent stage.
For the purpose of this project, Stages 1 through 10 are considered. This is because the the
scope of the project focuses on excavation induced movements.
4.2.5
Monitoring and Instrumentation Overview
The monitoring plan is a multidisciplinary task in place to ensure a safety and to observe phe-
nomena that may endanger surrounding buildings during station and tunnels construction, as
well as to alarm and take adequate mitigation actions, if necessary. The project is monitored
from the beginning of excavation for the top slab, until a few months after the completion of
the station.
In general, this project focuses on the monitoring data of the secant wall obtained from
the in-place inclinometers, for the horizontal deﬂections of the wall and the monitoring data
from the temporary bracing system from the strain gauges (load cells), which reveal information
on the forces acting in the struts. Figure 4.2.9 shows the monitoring plan layout, identifying
inclinometers as FB-IN## and the load cells as FB-LC-##.
Page 60
==PAGE:87==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.2.9: Instrumentation layout used in Frederiksberg.
4.2.5.1
Inclinometers
The inclinometers are placed within the secant pile and extend up to a depth of 32.9m and are
ﬁxed at this location. Three inclinometers are located within the longitudinal walls and one on
each of the transversal walls of the station. The lateral movements at the shorter sides should
be smaller because of the arching and three-dimensional eﬀects (Ou, 2006). Because the goal
is to identify the largest displacements, only inclinometers located on the long side of the main
box are interpreted, assuming two-dimensional plane strain behaviour (21, 22, 23 ; 25, 26 and
27). FB-IN29 was decommissioned early in the construction and has not been studied. The
following summarizes the characteristics of each inclinometers:
• INC 21 and 23
Located in the west side of the station in proximity of the Gymnasium and within the
double-secant pile wall, see Figure 4.2.7.
• INC 23
Located in the west side of the station in proximity of the Gymnasium and of a perpen-
dicular secant pile wall. The inclinometer is placed in the single-pile wall zone (Figure
4.2.7)
• INC 25
Located in the east side of the station. Due to its location, this inclinometer is considered
‘free-ﬁeld’ and it is located within the single-pile wall.
• INC 26 and 27
Located in the east side of the station next to the residential building.
Page 61
==PAGE:88==
Chapter 4. Stations
Apart for the lack of data for Stage 1, the inclinometers measurements present reliable data
for all other stages. The inclinometer distance from the temporary bracing system is shown in
Figure 4.2.10. FB-IN21 and 26 are located within the diameter of a strut.
Figure 4.2.10: Distance from inclinometers to struts.
4.2.5.2
Strain Gauges
The strut loads are measured with three sets of strain gauges on each side of the selected. The
struts selected are those which are critical and experience the highest loads in the design. The
unmonitored struts are not expected to be in a worse condition than the monitored ones.
The CMT designers chose speciﬁc struts to be monitored deemed appropriate to understand
the overall behaviour of the structure. The horizontal struts have the same characteristics and
similar level of action is expected in the central part of the station. The load cells are located
at the struts in axis D,F, H and K. All diagonal struts are monitored to understand the corner
behaviour. Figure 4.2.11 shows the location of the struts.
Figure 4.2.11: Position of strain gauges on struts/cross section (Metroselskabet, 2012o), showing the
FB-LC-A, B, C and D.

4.2.6
Observed Performance
The lateral wall movements developed during the construction stages at each depth are pre-
sented in Figure 4.2.12. The time elapse for all other inclinometers can be found in Appendix
C.3. Note that negative displacements are referred to as outward, towards the retained soil.
During the ﬁrst ﬁve stages (Stage 2 through 6), the steady rate of lateral movement observed
in the upper 6 measurements is of approximately 0.19mm/day. During this time, the wall de-
ﬂects with a cantilevered-like behaviour, however, once the third level of struts is installed, the
maximum displacements are found at deeper depths, closer to the excavation depths. The peak
displacement occurs during Stage 7: Excavation for third level of struts at a level of 11.9m in
the ML2 soil unit.
All inclinometers show the peak displacement during Stage 7, and a reduction in deformation
towards Stage 10, this may be attributed to the gain in strength of the struts and the stabilizing
of forces acting in the wall. However, the peak displacement is observed at a depth of 0.4m for
FB-IN21, 22 and 26. These inclinometers are located within the double secant wall and next
to the building structures which heavily inﬂuence the stiﬀness and behaviour of the wall at this
location (Hariri, 2016).

4.2.6.1
Lateral Wall Deformations
The lateral wall movements measured at FB-IN25 during construction are presented in Figure
4.2.13. Additional lateral deformation proﬁles are provided in Appendix C.3.1.
At shallow excavations, the lateral deformations at FB-IN25 were largely ‘cantilever’ shape
but tends to become prop-mode as excavation progresses. The peak displacements occur at a
distance of 14.9m below the surface. For inclinometers located in the West side of the excava-
tion, the maximum displacement is located at the head of the wall and are smaller than the
East wall. This is attributed to the basement of the Gymnasium, which seems to ‘increase’ the
stiﬀness of the walls.
Page 63
==PAGE:90==
Chapter 4. Stations
A clear discrepancy between locations is at FB-IN23, where a rotation point occurs at the
location of the ﬁrst level of struts; the wall deﬂects outwards above this point. Likewise, FB-
IN25 which is located across FB-IN23 also has a slight change in curvature at this location. This
may be attributed to a high strut stiﬀness.
Figure 4.2.13: Lateral wall movements at FB-IN25. Dashed red lines represent the excavation depth,
black dashed lines, the struts and thick black line shows the location of the top slab.
Figure 4.2.14 shows the wall deformation at Stage 10: Preparation of concrete level, previous
stages can be found in Appendix C.3.2.
The following is observed at the East inclinometers:
• During Stage 4, signiﬁcant movement towards the excavation occurs. This behaviour may
be in part due to the top slab shrinking after gaining considerable strength pulling the wall
inwards and the increase in lateral load during the installation of the ﬁrst level of struts;
• The ﬁxed connection with the top slab restrains lateral movement during Stages 6 through
9;
• The overall deﬂections are inward movements from the head up to a depth of z=-16m.
The ﬁeld data shows that the wall has a deep inward movement and the maximum lateral
deformations occur near the excavation surface, corresponding to the deformation behaviour of
a wall supported by high stiﬀness struts (Ou, 2006).

4.2.6.3
Bending Moment Distribution
The retaining walls at Frederiksberg are designed to have a ﬁxed connection between the wall
and the piles at the head. The Ftool model is presented in Figure 4.2.15, the uniform distributed
load is as speciﬁed in the Metroselskabet (2012c). The distributed load includes the self-weight
of the structure (8.77kPa) and temporary variable loads (15kPa).
Figure 4.2.15: Ftool model for Frederiksberg with a maximum moment at the ends of 746.4kNm.
As per that described in Section 3.2, the lateral wall deformation is presented in Figure
4.2.16 and the moment distributions for the pinned and ﬁxed conditions are presented in Figure
4.2.17. A ‘ﬁxed’ connection is never fully ﬁxed, and there will be some moment that is to be
carried by the slab. The behaviour of the wall is somewhere in between a pinned and a fully
ﬁxed connections presented below.
For a pinned connection, the maximum negative and positive bending moment are ≈-
663kNm/m at z=-28.5m and ≈590kNm/m at z=-15.0m, respectively; the fully ﬁxed connec-
tion yields maximum bending moments of ≈-746kNm/m at z=-28.9m and ≈632kNm/m at
z=-15.8m. These values are signiﬁcantly smaller than those presented by the designer (Met-
roselskabet, 2012c) correlating to the diﬀerence in displacements.

the peak displacements in the mentioned inclinometers.

4.2.7
Discussion of Performance
The following analysis seeks to identify major trends in the data. This investigation focuses on
the excavation induced movements. However, the activity after completion has an impact in the
lateral wall movements. Figure 4.2.19 presents the maximum lateral movement relative to the
maximum lateral deformation at the end of the project. The maximum lateral movement occurs
during Stage 14: Break in Track 1 at a depth of 14.9m. The lateral movement at the end of
Stage 10 accounts for the 58% of the maximum movement. The sudden increase in displacements
are related to the removal of struts and/or the breaking of tracks with TBMs.

Figure 4.2.19: Lateral deformation behaviour relative to construction progress.
Figure 4.2.20 shows the lateral wall movement versus excavation depth. An evident trend
is observed in the data.
Similar relationships of δhmax/He ratio reported by Clough and
O’Rourke (1990) ranged between 0.2% and 0.3%. Long (2001) found that for prop walls, the
average δhmax was 0.17%He. These authors investigated case histories with relatively shallow
excavations supported by ﬂexible walls, which usually present larger displacements. The use of
stiﬀsecant pile walls results in relatively small displacements (Ou, Hsieh, et al., 1993).
Figure 4.2.20: Observed maximum lateral wall deformations with respect to excavation depth.
The system stiﬀness and the lateral wall movements are studied for FB-IN25 and FB-IN23,
shown in Figure 4.2.21 and 4.2.22. The system stiﬀness is deﬁned by the following:
Page 69
==PAGE:96==
Chapter 4. Stations
• EI: bending stiﬀness of the retaining wall as per design:
EI=3313MPa;
• Es: stiﬀness of the soil layer at which the maximum deﬂection occur - Eur from Table
4.2.3;
• Eseq: equivalent soil stiﬀness as per deﬁned in Chapter 3, Section 3.3:
Eseq= 847MPa;
• havg: weighted average spacing between supports at any given stage.
The upper bound of the data set corresponds to FB-IN25, the lower bound corresponds to
FB-IN23. The data presents an evident trend - as the relative stiﬀness increases, so does the
displacement. For Frederiksberg, high relative stiﬀness is due to the small havg, corresponding
to the shallow excavations during the ﬁrst stages and the presence of soft ground all through
excavation.

4.2.8
Summary and Conclusions
Frederiksberg metro station is a 23.6m deep excavation supported by means of secant pile walls
with length of 26m. To reduce the impact of the construction in the Gymnasium and residential
building surrounding the site, part of the main box has been built with double secant piles.
The behaviour of the retaining walls are heavily inﬂuenced by the basement of the neighbour-
ing structures. The observed behaviour of the East wall follows a cantilevered-like deformation,
this rigidity is attributed to the increase in stiﬀness due to the nearby structures (Hariri, 2016).
In an eﬀort to evaluate the response of the wall without the inﬂuence of other structures,
FB-IN25 was extensively analyzed. The ﬁndings are summarized as:
• The upper and lower clay till are the dominant soil layers;
• The UCL is encountered at a depth of z=-21m;
• The δhmax=10.4mm at the end of excavation at FB-IN25 while all other inclinometers
showed smaller displacements;
• The δhmax/Hex ratio varies between 0.045-0.06Hex%;
• δhmax was located within the ML2 layer, at approximately 0.6Hex.
Moreover, the jumps in displacements coincide with the increase in measurements in the load
cells.
Page 71
==PAGE:98==
Chapter 4. Stations
4.3
Aksel Møllers Have
Aksel Møllers Have station (AMH) is located within the Copenhagen municipality of Fred-
eriksberg.
The station is constructed within a park with a residential building to the West
(distance < 10m) and a shallow building to the East, as seen in Figure 4.3.1. The residential
building is relevant for the retaining wall calculations due to its proximity to the excavation.
Figure 4.3.1: Aksel Møllers Have site shown framed in blue lines (taken from Google Earth).
4.3.1
Design Features
The wide underground station has a width of 16.8m between lining walls and a length of 61.5m
between head walls. The excavation is carried out by a hybrid bottom-up excavation. At the
initial stage of excavation, a top slab is casted to support the secant pile wall with struts at
either side; the excavation then proceeds as a typical bottom-up construction with three level
of struts as temporary supports designed to prevent any unacceptable settlements of the nearby
buildings. The typical cross section of the station is shown in Figure 4.3.2. The main design
features are summarized as follows (all levels are in m DVR90):
• Ground Level is at aprox. z=+11.14m;
• Area of the shaft is approximately 1170m2 (16.8x61.5m);
• Supported by reinforced secant pile walls with a cut oﬀdistance of 27m (embedment depth:
3.3m);
• Excavation level within the station at z=-12.55m (He = 23.7m);
• Main stair case to concourse level (z=+4.77m) is located in the northern end of the station.
Page 72
==PAGE:99==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.2: Typical cross section at Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012a).
4.3.2
Geotechnical Conditions
The site investigation at Aksel Møllers Have is carried out by means of geotechnical drilling,
in situ testing (SPT and HPDT) as well for geotechnical laboratory testing and geophysical
investigations. The borehole plan at AMH is presented in Figure 4.3.3. The investigation and
interpretation is presented in Metroselskabet (2012f). The main geotechnical characteristics of
the site are summarized below:
• The ﬁll thickness (FY) varies from 1-2m;
• The ﬁll is underlain by a 5-7m thick layer of upper clay till with sand till and sand (ML1);
• The ML1 layer is followed by a 7-11m thick layer of meltwater sand/gravel (DS/DG);
• The glacially disturbed zone of the limestone is approximately 1m thick at borehole C1402,
ranging to 2.8m at borehole C1405;
• Transition from UCL to MCL is located at approximately z=-15m;
• Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders.
Page 73
==PAGE:100==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.3: Borehole layout at Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012g).
Table 4.3.1: Soil and limestone at Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012f).
Page 74
==PAGE:101==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.4: Soil proﬁle at Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012g).
The borehole logs revealed a relatively homogeneous stratigraphy which is dominated by the
presence of the middle meltwater sand/silt unit (DS2/DG2). The Upper Copenhagen Limestone
is encountered at a relatively shallow depth and it is overlain by the DS2/DG2 layer and the
sporadic presence of lower clay till (ML2).
A detailed geological description is presented in
Appendix D.1.
4.3.2.1

Based on the results from the geotechnical investigations and considering that the stratigraphy is
relatively homogeneous, the designer assumes the design soil proﬁle in Table 4.3.2 for the design
of the retaining wall. Moreover, the characteristic soil parameters are presented in Table 4.3.3
and according to the GIR level III, the geological parameters vary between the values reported
in Table 4.3.4. The justiﬁcation for assessing the design parameters is presented in Appendix
D.2; the parameters are believed to be conservative by the designer.

4.3.2.2
Water Levels
According to speciﬁcations in GIR I and III, the groundwater levels shown in Table 4.3.5 should
be applied for the retaining wall design. In periods of high precipitation, the piezometric head
in the secondary aquifer can be at or even above the ground level. The primary aquifer is mainly
composed of Copenhagen limestone and Quarternary meltwater sand and gravel in hydraulic
connection with the limestone and has a regional extent in the Greater Copenhagen area. There
is also a large number of secondary aquifers, which may be isolated or in hydraulic connection
with each other and with the primary aquifer (Metroselskabet, 2012f).
Page 76
==PAGE:103==
Chapter 4. Stations
Table 4.3.5: Water levels at Aksel Møllers Have station (Metroselskabet, 2012f).
Similar to the design of other stations, the primary water table is considered for the SLS
and ULS. For the ALS analysis, the piezometric head in the primary and secondary aquifer is
considered to ensure a safe working place and the stability of structures.
During the project execution, a number of pumping wells are located in and around the
station box to maintain a dry site, with the GWL remaining at 1m below excavation level.
After completion and removal of temporary support system, the groundwater level is considered
to be located at the depth of excavation.
4.3.3
Retaining System Characteristics
Aksel Møllers Have permanent structures include the retaining wall consisting of single-line se-
cant piles extending up to a depth of 27m and a series of permanent slabs, cast after completion.
Retaining Wall System
A plan view of the station illustrating the arrangement of the pile walls is shown in Figure
4.3.5.
The continuous secant piles are constructed with primary and secondary piles.
The
main station has 1m diameter secant piles at 785 and 800mm horizontal spacing while 1100mm
spacing at the main entrance and emergency exit.
The main station secant piles have the
following characteristics:
• Length: 27m;
• Diameter: 1m;
• Horizontal spacing: 785/800mm (longitudinal/transversal wall);
• Moment of Inertia (785mm): 0.0599m4/m;
• Moment of Inertia (800mm): 0.0585m4/m;
• Young´s Modulus (primary and secondary piles): 33GPa (C30/37).
Page 77
==PAGE:104==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.5: Secant pile conﬁguration at Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012a).
Permanent Slabs
The retaining wall is supported in its permanent state by the interior structures, which includes
slabs at diﬀerent levels of the station.
In the permanent stage, only the roof slab will be
connected to the retaining walls and is allowed to act in tension/compression. The thickness of
the slabs are summarized below:
• Roof Level: Varies - with an equivalent area of Aeq = 0.67m2/m;
• Concourse Level: 0.62m;
• Technical Level: 0.40m;
• Intermediate Level: 1.8m;
• Platform Level: 0.25m;
• Below Platform Level: Varies.
4.3.3.1
Temporary Support Systems
Three level of struts are installed from axis C to J (Figure 4.3.6) while four level of struts are
placed at the left and right of the top slab (Figure 4.3.7). The struts are designed to prevent
any excessive settlement during construction and are kept in compression by means of hydraulic
jacks during the construction phase are used at AMH. The steel tubes used during construction
have the following characteristics:
• Geometry
Station - Ø813x25mm
Main Entrance - Ø610x20mm
• Spacing
Station - 5.5m
Main Entrance - 4.5m
• Moment of Inertia
Station - 0.004805 m4/m
Main Entrance - 0.001612 m4/m
All struts have a Young’s Modulus of Es = 210MPa. After installation, a prestressing force
of 550kN is applied to each strut.

4.3.4
Construction Sequence
The executive phases of construction of the main box at Aksel Møllers Have deﬁned by the
designer and presented in ‘General RW Calculation Report’(Metroselskabet, 2012a) are summa-
rized below:
• Stage 1
Excavation to level z = +9.75m and construction of secant pile walls;
• Stage 2
Excavation to level z = +7.55m and casting of the top slab at level z = +9.30 between
axes C and J. On the left and right sides of the slab, temporary bracing system is installed
at z = +8.57m and z = +9.59m, see Figure 4.3.7;
• Stage 3
Excavation to level z = +2.30m followed by the installation of the ﬁrst level of temporary
bracing at z = +3.80m;
• Stage 4
Excavation to level z = −2.70m followed by the installation of the second level of struts
at z = −1.20m;
• Stage 4
Excavation to level z = −8.0m followed by the installation of the third level of struts at
z = −6.50m;
• Stage 5
Excavation to level z = −12.45m to underside the bottom slab, ensuring the dewatering
is maintained 1m below the working level;
Page 79
==PAGE:106==
Chapter 4. Stations
• Stage 6
Preparation of the lean concrete level, application of the waterproof membrane and casting
of the foundation slab at level z = −10.65m;
• Stage 7
Removal of the third level of steel struts and casting of lining walls;
• Stage 8
Construction of the intermediate slab and the installation of temporary columns. Once the
intermediate slab concrete has reached its design strength, the TBMs enter the stations;
• Stage 9
Removal of the second level of struts and construction of the technical level;
• Stage 10
Removal of the ﬁrst level of struts and construction of the concourse level;
• Stage 11
Demolition of temporary columns, construction of the roof slab and backﬁlling.
It is ensured during excavation that dewatering is maintained 1m below the working level.

The end of each stage is deﬁned by the day prior to the start date of the following stage. The

4.3.5
Monitoring and Instrumentation Overview
The investigation focuses on the observations of horizontal deformations of the secant wall
conducted by means of inclinometers and in the monitoring data for the temporary bracing
system from the strain gauges, which reveals information on the forces acting in the struts.
Figure 4.3.8 shows the monitoring plan layout, identifying inclinometers as AMH-IN## and
the load cells as AMH-LC-##.
Figure 4.3.8: Instrumentation layout in Aksel Møllers Have.
4.3.5.1
Inclinometers
The horizontal displacements of the retaining walls are monitored with the use of inclinometers.
Eight inclinometers are installed in AMH as seen in Figure 4.3.8. The inclinometers are anchored
up to two meters below the toe of the wall and the heads are protected by steel covers.
The deformation behaviour at the central section of the shorter sides, aﬀected by concrete
arching eﬀect, is three-dimensional and the displacement should be much smaller (Ou, 2006),
Page 81
==PAGE:108==
Chapter 4. Stations
for this reason only the inclinometers on the long side of the wall are considered, assuming
plane-strain conditions. The following summarizes the characteristics of the inclinometers:
• INC 21
No data for Stage 1 and 17. Located within the A and C axis, the head of the pile is not
supported by the top slab. No 0.4m measurement.
• INC 22
No data for is available Stage 1 and 17. Located within the top slab and all measurements
are available.
• INC 23
No data is available for Stages 1, 16 and 17. Located within the top slab and there are
double pile walls at this location. Inclinometer extents up to -25.4m, 1.6m above the toe
of the wall and its ﬁxity cannot be conﬁrmed nor assumed.
• INC 25
No data is available for Stages 1 and 17. Located within the top slab and there are double
pile walls at this location. Inclinometer extents up to -28.4m. No 0.4m measurement. The
inclinometer is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’.
• INC 26
No data for is available Stage 1 and 17. Located within the top slab and all measurements
are available. The inclinometer is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’.
• INC 27
No data for is available Stage 1, 17, 18, 19, 20 and 21.
Located within the A and C
axis, the head of the pile is not supported by the top slab. The inclinometer is considered
‘free-ﬁeld’.
Apart for the lack of data for several stages, the inclinometers measurements show reliable
for all other stages and provide a very useful record. Figure 4.3.9 shows the inclinometer distance
from the temporary bracing system.

4.3.6
Observed Performance
The monitoring data from the inclinometers mentioned in the previous section has been pro-
cessed and it revealed that the displacements were overall larger at AMH-IN26, this inclinometer
is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’ and it is good representation of the behaviour of the other inclinome-
ters. The cumulative displacement at AMH-IN26 is presented in Figure 4.3.11, based on the
construction timeline in Table 4.3.6. Additional ﬁgures can be found in Appendix D.3.
At shallow excavations and early stages, there is a cantilevered behaviour and the maximum
displacements are recorded at the head of the wall (δh < 0.6mm). At Stage 3: Excavation for
ﬁrst level of struts, a steady increase in displacement is observed at level 7.4m (DS unit), the
rate of displacement up to the end of Stage 5: Excavation of second level of struts, after which
the displacements stabilize, is around 0.11mm/day.
While the displacements at a depth of 13.4m (DS unit) remain small (δh < 2.9mm) prior to
the end of Stage 4: Installation of ﬁrst level of struts, the ﬁnal largest displacement at the end
of Stage 10 occur within this level. Another drastic increase in displacement of this nature is
observed during Stage 6: Installation of second level of struts. This behaviour is attributed to
the prestressing of the struts which occurs sometime after installation and produces an abrupt
change in the stress ﬁeld behind the retaining wall. As expected, the displacements close to the
toe of the wall are minimal until the excavation proceeds to deeper depths.
Similar behaviour is observed in AMH-IN22 and 23 although the displacements here are
much smaller. AMH-21 and 27, which are not supported at the head by the top slab, reveal
disturbances on their measurements at the end of Stage 10: Preparation of concrete level. These
displacements shall be used with care.
Page 83
==PAGE:110==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.11: Lateral wall movements occurring during construction at AMH-IN26.
4.3.6.1
Lateral Wall Deﬂections
The lateral wall movements measured at AMH-IN26 during construction are presented in Figure
4.3.12. Additional lateral deformation proﬁles are provided in Appendix D.3.1.
Apart for Stages 2 the shape of the deﬂected shape corresponds to a prop-mode deformation,
with a relatively large displacement at the location of the top slab (δh = 1 −5mm).
The
deformation at all inclinometers are similar with diﬀerence in the magnitude in displacement.
At shallow depths, the maximum displacements occur close to excavation, while at deeper depths
the maximum displacement remains at the mid-height of the wall, along the middle meltwater
sand layer.
Page 84
==PAGE:111==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.12: Lateral Wall Movements at AMH-IN26. Dashed red lines represent the excavation depth,
black dashed lines, the struts and thick black line shows the location of the top slab.
Figure 4.3.13 superimposes the lateral wall movements for all inclinometers at the end of
Stage 10: Preparation of concrete level, previous stages can be found in Appendix D.3.2. After
the casting of the slab (between Stage 3 and 4) there seems to be a pull inwards at the head
of the wall possibly produced by the shrinkage and creep movements of the top slab. In the
subsequent stages however, the top slab restrains the movement of the top keeping these dis-
placements relatively constant at all inclinometers, except at AMH-21 and 27.
At the end of Stage 10, the maximum lateral movement is located within the DS layer at a
depth of 13.4m, 10m above the ﬁnal excavation depth. As observed, AMH-22, 26 and 27 have
similar deﬂected shape up to a depth of 10m, after which there is a diﬀerence in displacements.
The smallest displacements were recorded by AMH-21 and 25, the latter has larger displacements
close to the toe of the wall.

may be attributed to the fact that a strut provided a sharp increase in lateral pressure and the
wall deforms accordingly, while the earth pressure provides a more gradual support, and as the
soil is excavated the change in pressure is smooth, so are the displacements. This phenomena
can also observed as the ‘jumps’ in the time elapse.

4.3.6.3
Bending Moment Distribution
The retaining walls at AMH are designed to have a ﬁxed connection between the wall and the
piles at the head. The Ftool model is presented in Figure 4.3.14, the uniform distributed load
is as speciﬁed in the Metroselskabet (2012a) with a self-weight of 10kPa and variable loads of
15kPa.
Page 87
==PAGE:114==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.14: Ftool model for Aksel Møllers Have with a moment at the ﬁxed ends of 792.2kNm.
The moment distribution is obtained by diﬀerentiating twice the polynomial function simu-
lating the deformation curve, as discussed in Section 3.2. The deﬂected shape measured in Aksel
Møllers Have considering the inclinometers in the East side is presented in Figure 4.3.15 and its
moment distribution in Figure 4.3.16. A ‘ﬁxed’ connection is never truly fully ﬁxed, and there
will be some moment that is to be carried by the slab. The behaviour of the wall is somewhere
in between a pinned and a fully ﬁxed connections presented below.
For a pinned connection, the maximum negative and positive bending moment are ≈-
430kNm/m at z=-13.7m and ≈380kNm/m at z=-25m, respectively, while the fully ﬁxed con-
nection yields maximum bending moments of ≈-415kNm/m at z=-12.7m and ≈310kNm/m at
z=-25m. These moments are well below those computed by the designer (Metroselskabet, 2012a),
and this correlates with the discrepancy in displacements.
Figure 4.3.15: Sixth-order polynomial function describing the end of Stage 10.
Page 88
==PAGE:115==
Chapter 4. Stations
(a) Pinned connection
(b) Fixed connection
Figure 4.3.16: Bending Moment Distribution.
4.3.6.4
Strut Performance
The load history for load cell D (AMH-LC-D) is presented in Figure 4.3.17 and load C in Figure
4.3.18. The monitored struts are located in the proximity of AMH-IN27 and 26.
For Load cell D, the load at the ﬁrst level struts (or level 0) (z = −1.20m) stabilizes during
the installation of the second level of struts (z = −5.95m). This coincides with the fact that at
shallow depths, the lateral movements stabilize after Stage 4. The struts at level 0 and 1 record
similar loads, with a peak load during construction of 1200kN. Strut Level 2 (z = −10.95m)
and 3 (z = −16.25m) recorded the largest forces and the maximum displacement of the wall
was detected between these two struts. The loads keep increasing after the excavation stage is
done, but the largest forces recorded are similar at 2200kN.
Load Cell C is located within the top slab, however, it is evident that the three levels of
struts present a similar behaviour than those monitored by Load Cell D. The load in Strut Level
1 stabilizes quite early in the construction stage (Stage 5: Excavation for 2nd level of struts)
and remains with a relatively constant load of 900kN, the displacements at this depth were also
smallest recorded.
While the increase in strength of the struts coincide with the increase in displacement in
Stage 6 and 8 in AMH-IN26, this behaviour is not present at AMH-IN27, regardless of its
proximity to the braces. AMH-IN27 is located at a distance of 9.2m from the nearest corner
and three-dimensional eﬀects could have inﬂuenced the response of the wall to the pre-load at
this location.

==PAGE:116==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.17: Load cell D: strut load changes during construction.
Figure 4.3.18: Load cell C: strut load changes during construction.

4.3.7
Discussion of Performance
The following analysis seeks to identify major trends in the monitoring data. The investiga-
tion focuses in the excavation induced movements, but activity after completion will have an
impact on the structure.
Figure 4.3.19 presents the maximum lateral movement relative to
the maximum lateral deformation at the end of the project. The maximum lateral movement
(δhmax = 13.0mm) occurs during Stage 16: Break in Track 2 at a depth of 16.4m and the
‘jump’ in displacement is attributed to the removal of the 3rd level of struts, which is a common
behaviour. However, the lateral movement at the end of Stage 10 accounts for the 73% of the
maximum movement; the displacements occurred during excavation, which is higher compared
to other Cityringen stations. The signiﬁcant change in lateral movement shown in Figure 4.3.19
is followed by the removal of the third level of struts.

Figure 4.3.19: Lateral deformation behaviour relative to construction progress.
Figure 4.3.20 presents the normalized lateral wall movement versus excavation depth. In
this ﬁgure, the upper and lower limit correspond to the measured for AMH-IN26 and 22. The
relationships found here are among the lowest the Cityringen station interpreted for this report.
An evident trend is observed in the data. Similar relationships of δhmax/He ratio reported
by Clough and O’Rourke (1990) ranged between 0.2% and 0.3%. Long (2001) found that for
prop walls, the average δhmax were 0.17%He, whereas Moormann (2004) ﬁndings are closer to
that of Clough and O’Rourke (1990), the average value is δhmax/He = 0.27%, for AMH this
ratio was as low as 0.03%He.
The ratio δhmax/He was approximately 0.06% at the end of Stage 6: Installation of 2nd level
of struts, which is much larger than the other stages possibly owed to the large unsupported
length at this stage.
Page 91
==PAGE:118==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.20: Observed maximum lateral wall deformations with respect to excavation depth.
Further analysis leads to the relationship of the system stiﬀness to the lateral wall movements,
shown in Figure 4.3.21 and 4.3.22. The system stiﬀness is deﬁned by the following:
• EI: bending stiﬀness of the retaining wall as per design:
EI=1977MPa;
• Es: stiﬀness of the soil layer at which the maximum deﬂection occur - Eur from Table
4.3.3.
• Eseq: equivalent soil stiﬀness as per deﬁned in Chapter 3, Section 3.3:
Eseq= 612.2MPa;
• havg: weighted average spacing between supports at any given stage.
The lower values correspond to AMH-IN22 and the higher to AMH-IN26. The height system
stiﬀness are attributed to the shallow excavations (small havg), with the largest displacements
occurring at ‘weak’ soils (FY).
There is a large scatter in the data but there seems to be increasing displacements to relative
stiﬀness, for both ρ∗and ρeq. The relative stiﬀness increases if the denominator decreases, which
means that either the location of the soil layer at which the maximum displacement occur is
weak or there is a small havg. It is to be noted that the range of the normalized displacement
is 0.04, reinforcing the idea that wall stiﬀness and supporting system has an insigniﬁcant eﬀect
on the wall and ground movements (Moormann, 2004).
Page 92
==PAGE:119==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.3.21: Relative Stiﬀness compared to normalized displacements.
Figure 4.3.22: Relative Equivalent Stiﬀness compared to normalized displacements.
4.3.8
Summary and Conclusions
Aksel Møllers Have metro station has an excavation depth of 23.7m with 27m long secant pile
walls. The stratigraphy of the site is comprise mainly of DS (meltwater sand). However, the
UCL is encountered at a relatively shallow depth (z=-14.8m), giving the system a high equivalent
stiﬀness, Eeq. The following summarizes the results of the analysis:
• The δhmax varied between 5.2-8.6mm at the end of excavation with the largest displace-
ments occurring at AMH-IN23 and 26;
• The δhmax/Hex ratio varies between 0.03-0.05%Hex
• δhmax was located within the DS (meltwater sand) layer, at approximately 0.6Hex.
All observed performances in the six inclinometers were comparable. The minimum dis-
placement was recorded at AMH-IN25 and may be attributed to the double pile at this location.
Page 93
==PAGE:120==
Chapter 4. Stations
The second least displacements are recorded by AMH-IN21 and 27. These two inclinometers
are located close to the corner of the excavation and because of arching eﬀects, wall deﬂections
at this location may be smaller than those at the central section (Tan et al., 2011).
The system stiﬀness show an increasing relationship of relative system stiﬀness to displace-
ment. However, Stage 2 measurements did not ﬁt the general trend of the system stiﬀness and
may be explained by the shallow excavation depth and the small distance between the top slab
and the excavation depth.
Page 94
==PAGE:121==
Chapter 4. Stations
4.4
Nuuks Plads
Nuuks Plads Station (NUP) is located along the road of Jagtvej and there are buildings located
to the East and South of the station, as seen in Figure 4.4.1. A residential building is located
at a distance > 20m north of the station.
Figure 4.4.1: Nuuks Plads site shown in blue lines (taken from Google Earth).
4.4.1
Design Features
The wide underground station has a width of 16.8m between lining walls and a length of 61.5m
between head walls. The excavation is carried out by a hybrid bottom-up excavation. At the
initial stage of excavation, a top slab is casted to support the secant pile wall, the excavation then
proceeds as a typical bottom-up construction with three level of struts as temporary supports
designed to prevent any unacceptable settlements of the nearby buildings. The main design
features are summarized as follows (all levels are in m DVR90):
• Ground Level is at approx. z=+7.7m;
• Area of the shaft is approximately 1000m2 (61.5x16.8m);
• Reinforced secant pile walls with a cut oﬀdistance of 27m (embedment depth: 4.5m);
• Excavation level within the station at z≈-16.5m (He = 22.5m);
• Main stair case to concourse level is located in the northern end of the station.
4.4.2
Geotechnical Conditions
The results of the geotechnical investigation and interpretation for Nuuks Plads is summarized
in the ‘Nuuks Plads - Geotechnical interpretative Report’ (Metroselskabet, 2012t). Relevant
characteristics of the site are summarized as:
• The ﬁll thickness (FY) varies from 1-4m, from South to North;
• The ﬁll is underlain by a 4-8m thick layer of upper clay till (ML);
• The ML layer is followed by a 3-6m thick layer of meltwater sand and gravel (DS/DG);
• The limestone layer underlies the DS/DG and the thickness of glacially disturbed zone is
≈2m;
• Transition from UCL to MCL is located at approximately z=-21.2m;
• Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders.
Page 95
==PAGE:122==
Chapter 4. Stations
The borehole plan used for the site investigation for Nuuks Plads is shown in Figure 4.4.2.
The ground conditions at the construction site have been summarized in Table 4.4.1 and Figure
4.4.3. The individual layers were identiﬁed by employing geological descriptions, classiﬁcation
tests, laboratory and geotechnical/geophysical in situ tests.
Figure 4.4.2: Borehole layout plan at Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012s).
Table 4.4.1: Soil and limestone at Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012s).
Page 96
==PAGE:123==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.4.3: Layering of soil and limestone at Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012s).
The borehole logs revealed a thick layer of upper clay/sand till (ML1/MS2) which thickness
increases from South to North.
A layer of meltwater sand interposed in the upper clay till
unit was found in boring C1318, this layer is combined with the DS/DG/MS unit in the design
proﬁles. Moreover, a thin layer (< 0.5m) of lower sand till (MS2) was also found in C1318 over-
laying the limestone and has been included in the DS/DG unit. The Copenhagen Limestone
units have consistent thickness throughout the station.
There is a thin meltwater silt unit (DI) which is not shown in Figure 4.4.3 as the thicknesses
and extents are limited. A very thin layer of very clayey silt are found below the upper clay
till layer, with a thickness of approximately 0.5m. Due to the minimal occurrence of the layer
combined with the layer’s characteristics being similar to the very silty clay till the silt has been
included in the ML/MS unit.
The detailed geological description is summarized in Appendix E.1.
4.4.2.1
Design Proﬁles
The lower and upper bound characteristic parameters are selected as estimates of the values
aﬀecting the occurrence of the relevant limit state. The designer states that these shall be used
as most unfavourable for the occurrence of the limit state being considered. The designer has
used all three design proﬁles as given in Table 4.4.2. Preliminary designs of the retaining wall
proved that the most critical proﬁle is that in Table 4.4.3; the characteristic design parameters
are presented in Table 4.4.4.
A justiﬁcation presented by the designer regarding the design
parameters is summarized in Appendix E.2.
The results of additional soil investigation along with sensitivity analyses performed conﬁrm
the validity of assumption made for selection of design parameters. The design of the retaining
wall based on the chosen geotechnical design parameters is conservative enough to assure a safe
working place and stability of structures as well for the surrounding buildings (Metroselska-
Page 97
==PAGE:124==
Chapter 4. Stations
bet, 2012s).
Table 4.4.2: Soil design proﬁles at Nuuks Plads station (Metroselskabet, 2012s).

4.4.2.2
Water Levels
The groundwater levels shown in Table 4.4.5 should be applied for the retaining wall design. In
periods of high precipitation, the piezometric head in the secondary aquifer can be at or even
above the ground level.
Similar to the design of other stations, the primary water table is considered for the SLS
and ULS analyses for the secondary water table is in close proximity. For the ALS analysis, the
piezometric head in the primary and secondary aquifer is considered to ensure a safe working
place and the stability of structures.
The primary aquifer is mainly composed of Copenhagen limestone and Quarternary melt-
water sand and gravel in hydraulic connection with the limestone and has a regional extent in
the Greater Copenhagen area. There is also a large number of secondary aquifer, which may be
isolated or in hydraulic connection with each other and with the primary aquifer (Metroselska-
bet, 2012s).
During the project execution, a number of pumping wells are located in and around the
station box to maintain a dry site, with the GWL remaining at 1m below excavation level.
After completion and removal of temporary support system, the groundwater level is considered
to be located at the depth of excavation. The retaining structures are designed to withstand
the full hydrostatic water pressure acting behind the walls.
Table 4.4.5: Water levels at Nuuks Plads station (Metroselskabet, 2012s).
4.4.2.3
Permanent Structures
The permanent structure at Nuuks Plads station include the retaining wall, a single-line secant
piles wall, extending up to a depth of 27m and a series of permanent slabs, cast after completion.
Retaining Wall System
A plan view of the station illustrating the pile walls is shown in Figure 4.4.4. The continuous
diaphragm is constructed by means of secant piles with the following characteristics:
• Length: 27m (with 1.65m of backﬁll above the head);
• Diameter: 1m;
• Horizontal spacing: 785/800mm (longitudinal/transversal wall);
• Moment of Inertia (785mm): 0.06259m4/m;
• Moment of Inertia (800mm): 0.061328m4/m;
• Young´s Modulus (primary and secondary piles): 33GPa (C30/37).
Page 99
==PAGE:126==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.4.4: Secant pile conﬁguration at Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012e).
Permanent Slabs
The retaining wall is supported in its permanent state by the interior structures, which includes
slabs at diﬀerent levels of the station. The thickness of the slabs are summarized below:
• Roof Level: Varies with an equivalent thickness of teq = 0.67m/m
• Concourse Level: 0.62m
• Technical Level: 0.40m
• Intermediate Level: 1.8m
• Platform Level: 0.25m
• Below Platform Level: Varies
In the permanent stage, only the roof slab will be connected to the retaining walls and is
allowed to act in tension/compression.
4.4.2.4
Temporary Support Systems
Three level of struts at Nuuks Plads are used to prevent any excessive settlement during con-
struction and are kept in compression by means of hydraulic jacks during the construction phase.
All struts have a Young’s Modulus of Es = 210MPa. After installation, a prestressing force of
550kN is applied to each strut. A plan view and cross section illustrating the station layout are
presented in Figures 4.4.5 and 4.4.6.The steel tubes used during construction have the following
characteristics:
• Geometry

Main Entrance - 4.5m
Emergency Exit - 4.0m
• Moment of Inertia
Station - 0.004805 m4/m

4.4.3
Construction Sequence
The executive phases of construction of the main box of Nuuks Plads were presented in ‘General
RW Calculation Report’(Metroselskabet, 2012e) and summarized below:
• Stage 1
Excavation from the general level z = +7.6m to z = +7.1m and construction of secant
pile walls;
• Stage 2
Excavation to level z = +3.76m and casting of the permanent top slab at z = +4.95m to
support the retaining walls;
• Stage 3
Excavation to level z = −2.41m followed by the installation of the ﬁrst level of steel struts
at z = −0.50m;
• Stage 4
Excavation to level z = −7.16m followed by the installation of the second level of tempo-
rary bracing at z = −5.22m;
• Stage 5
Excavation to level z = −12.63m followed by the installation of the third level of struts at
z = −10.72m;
• Stage 6
Final excavation to level z = −16.56m for realization of the bottom slab;
• Stage 7
Preparation of the lean concrete level, application of waterproof membrane and realization
of foundation slab at z = −14.5m;
• Stage 8
Removal of the third level of struts and casting of lining walls;
• Stage 9
Installation of temporary columns to support intermediate and above level slabs until the
end of the internal structure construction and realization of intermediate slab;
• Stage 10
Removal of second level of struts and realization of the technical level;
• Stage 11
Removal of ﬁrst level of struts and realization of the concourse level;
• Stage 12
Demolition of temporary columns and ﬁnalization of roof slab and backﬁlling.
It is ensured during excavation that dewatering is maintained 1m below the working level.
4.4.3.1

The deformation analysis relies heavily in the proper identiﬁcation of the construction time-
line. The timeline is based on the construction sequence proposed by the designer as well for
the construction progress information provided by the CMT engineers at Metroselskabet. The
construction timeline used for the analysis is presented in Table 4.4.6.

The end of a stage is deﬁned as the day prior to the start date of the following stage. The
start date of the installation of the struts corresponds to the day the monitoring software Kronos
started recording measurements, while the end date corresponds to the date when the load of
the struts stabilized. The excavation stages are assumed to occur between the installation of
struts, but it is to be noted that the excavation is an on-going process: the excavations proceeds
as the struts are being installed.
For the purpose of this project, Stages 1 through 10 are considered. This is because the
scope of the project focuses in excavation induced movements.
4.4.4
Monitoring and Instrumentation Overview
The investigation focuses on the monitoring data from the in-place inclinometers, for the hor-
izontal deﬂections of the wall and the monitoring data for the temporary bracing system from
the strain gauges, which reveal information on the forces acting in the struts.

shows the monitoring plan layout, identifying inclinometers as NUP-IN## and the load cells as
NUP-LC-##.

Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.4.7: Instrumentation layout in Nuuks Plads
4.4.4.1
Inclinometers
The inclinometers are placed within the secant pile and extend up to a depth of 31.4m and
32.4m depending on the inclinometer. Because the inclinometer extends several meters below
the toe of the wall, it has been assumed that its tip is ﬁxed.
Three inclinometers are located within the longitudinal walls and one on each of the transver-
sal walls of the station, as seen in Figure 4.4.7. The deformation behaviour at the central section
of the shorter sides, aﬀected by concrete arching eﬀect, is three-dimensional and the displace-
ment should be much smaller (Ou, 2006), for this reason only the inclinometers on the long
side of the wall are considered. Furthermore, NUP-IN25, 26 and 27 have been installed outside
the secant pile within the soil layer and will not be investigated. The following summarizes the
characteristics of the inclinometers:
INC 21, 22 and 23
• Located at the northwest of the excavation, next to Jagtvej;
• Recording of measurements begin on June 17, 2013, just prior to the end of the excavation
of the top slab (June 25, 2013);
• No data corresponding for Stages 1: Excavation for top slab, Stages 17: Intermediate slab
casted, Stages 19: Technical level and Stages 21: Concourse slab casted;
• Inclinometer extends up to 4.4m below the toe of the wall and are ﬁxed at this location.
Apart for the lack of data for several stages, the inclinometers measurements show reliable
for all other stages and provide a useful record. The inclinometer distance from the temporary
bracing system is shown in Figure 4.4.8.

4.4.4.2
Strain Gauges
The CMT designers chose speciﬁc struts to be monitored shown in Figure 4.4.9. These struts
are deemed appropriate to understand the overall behaviour of the structure. In accordance to
that presented by the designer, on all three strut levels, 8 out of 13 struts are equipped with
strain gauges, in order to monitor the axial loads. The struts monitored are the external ones
which are subjected to the highest loads (A and D), as well for two struts next to them, these
are subject to loads very similar to the ones of non-monitored struts.
Figure 4.4.9: Monitored struts at Nuuks Plads. Load cells are shown in red.
4.4.5
Observed Performance
The behaviour of the wall in the northwest was captured by three inclinometers where the largest
deformations were observed at NUP-IN22 and 23. The cumulative displacements at NUP-IN23
are presented in Figure 4.4.10, based on the construction timeline in Table 4.4.6. Additional
ﬁgures can be found in Appendix E.3. Note that positive (inward) displacements are towards
Page 105
==PAGE:132==
Chapter 4. Stations
the excavation.
There is a slight inward movement of the wall during Stages 1 and 2, but the displacement
are small (δh < 0.5mm). During Stage 3: Excavation for ﬁrst level of struts, there is marginal
increase in displacements at level 10.4m, within the upper clay till (ML) layer. The following is
observed within this level:
• Steady inward displacements up to the end of Stage 7: Excavation for third level of struts;
• Between Stage 3 and, the rate of displacement remains at 0.06mm/day;
• The movement stabilizes at the end of Stage 7 and remains relatively constant during the
subsequent stages ( δh ∼6mm).
Meanwhile, at depths 13.4m (DS/DG) and 16.4m (UCL I), the displacements remain small
(δh < 1.0mm) up to Stage 6: Installation of second level of struts, at which the excavation
depth is 14.23m. After the excavation proceeds to deeper depths, the displacements at these
two levels increases. The maximum rate of displacement occurs during Stage 7 at approximately
0.19mm/day. Again, the displacements increase slightly and stabilize at the end of Stage 8: Fi-
nal excavation (δh ∼8.8mm).
While a similar behaviour is observed in NUP-IN21 (Appendix E.3, Figure E.3.1), the dis-
placements at this location are somewhat smaller. Overall, both inclinometers show comparable
results. NUP-IN22 (Appendix E.3, Figure E.3.2) reveal comparable behaviour up to Stage 6,
at which a deep outward movement is observed, however, the maximum displacement is still
located between the depths of 13.4-16.4m.

4.4.5.1
Lateral Wall Deformations
The lateral wall deformations are those of the end displacement at a given stage. After analysis
of the cumulative displacement in Figure 4.4.10, it is concluded that the end displacement at each
stage represent the overall behaviour of the structure. The lateral wall movements measured at
NUP-IN23 during construction are presented in Figure 4.4.11. Additional lateral deformation

proﬁles are provided in Appendix E.3.1.
Apart for stages 1 and 2, the shape of the deﬂected shape corresponds to a prop-mode
deformation. This behaviour is observed in NUP-IN21 while NUP-IN22 behaves similarly up
to the end of Stage 6, as previously mentioned, and has a clear outward movement at the
location of the top slab which may be owed to the connection of the top slab with the wall
and the redistribution of moment through the pile cap. The maximum displacement for all
inclinometers was located at the same depth, consistently.

NUP-IN21 and 23 present a slight change in curvature at approx z=-4m which is attributed the
ﬁxed connection at the top slab which may produce a slight rotation at the head of the piles. It
is to be noted that the proximity of NUP-IN23 to the corner of the main excavation does not
seem to aﬀect the magnitude of its displacements.

4.4.5.3
Bending Moment Distribution
At Nuuks Plads, the connection between the retaining walls and the top slab was ﬁxed. However,
for the purpose of this analysis both connections are investigated. The structural model used in
Ftool is shown in Figure 4.4.13 and the material properties and the loads are as prescribed by
the designer and summarized in Section 4.4.2.3. The distributed load includes the self-weight of
the structure (5kPa) and temporary variable loads (15kPa).
Figure 4.4.13: Ftool model for Nuuks Plads: maximum moment at the ﬁxed ends, 570.4kNm.
The lateral wall deformation is presented in Figure 4.4.14 showing the measurements for the
‘free-ﬁeld’ inclinometers. Following the methodology presented in Section 3.2 the moment dis-
tributions for the pinned and ﬁxed conditions are computed and presented in Figure 4.4.15. A
‘ﬁxed’ connection is never fully ﬁxed, and there will be some moment that is to be carried by the
slab and part of it to be transferred to the pile and redistributed in the pile cap. The behaviour
of the wall is then somewhere in between a pinned and a fully ﬁxed connections presented below.
For a pinned connection, the maximum negative and positive bending moment are ≈-
366kNm/m at z=-27.5m and ≈364kNm/m at z=-15.8m, respectively; the fully ﬁxed connec-
tion yields maximum bending moments within the wall of ≈-926kNm/m at z=-27.3m and
≈619kNm/m at z=-15.1m. The approximated moments are well below the values calculated
by the designer (Metroselskabet, 2012e); however this method of approximation may lead to
deviations from the actual situation. Based on the measured wall displacements, the moment is
expected to be lower.
Page 109
==PAGE:136==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.4.14: Sixth-order polynomial function for the end of Stage 10.
(a) Pinned connection
(b) Fixed connection
Figure 4.4.15: Bending Moment Distribution at Nuuks Palds.
4.4.5.4
Strut Performance
The load history for load cell D (NUP-LC-D) is presented in Figure 4.4.16. Figures for load
cells A and B can be found in Appendix E.3.3. The monitored strut is located in proximity of
NUP-IN23. The maximum loads were recorded at these cells, as predicted for the monitoring
plan.
Page 110
==PAGE:137==
Chapter 4. Stations
The load at the ﬁrst level struts (installed at z = −6.6m) stabilizes during the installation
of the second level of struts (installed at z = −12.3m). This coincides with the fact that after
Stage 6, there is not a signiﬁcant change in displacement at depths shallower than 10m. The
load at strut levels 2 and 3 (z = −12.3m and −17.8m) stabilize during Stage 10, agreeing with
the relatively constant displacements during this time. The peak loads for Levels 1, 2 and 3 are
1400, 2500 and 3400kN, respectively.
While a similar behaviour is observed in Load cells A and B (in proximity of NUP-IN21),
the cells recorded smaller loads. The peak load for Levels 1, 2 and 3 are 1200, 1700 and 2900kN,
respectively. Smaller displacements are seen in NUP-IN23 in comparison to NUP-IN21 in the
early stages. However, after Stage 7: Excavation for 3rd level of struts the displacements at
these locations are virtually equal, still forces at Load Cell B are slightly smaller.
Figure 4.4.16: Load Cell D: strut load changes during construction.
4.4.6
Discussion of Performance
The following analysis seeks to identify major trends in the data. As mentioned before, this
investigation focused in the excavation induced movements, but it is known that activity after
completion will have an impact on the structure. Figure 4.4.17 presents the maximum lateral
movement relative to the maximum lateral deformation at the end of the project. The maximum
lateral movement (δhmax = 12.3m) occurs during Stage 19: Technical level at a depth of 16.4m.
The lateral movement at the end of Stage 10 accounts for the 63% of the maximum movement.
The drastic change in displacement shown in Figure 4.4.17 is due to the removal of the third
level of struts; after this there is little increase in displacements.

Figure 4.4.17: Lateral deformation behaviour relative to construction progress.
Figure 4.4.18 presents the normalized lateral wall movement versus excavation depth. An
evident trend is observed in the data. Similar relationships of δhmax/He ratio reported by Clough
and O’Rourke (1990) ranged between 0.2% and 0.3%. Long (2001) found that for prop walls,
the average δhmax were 0.17%He. In this ﬁgure, the upper and lower limit correspond to the
measured for NUP-IN23 and 22 and the limit of the ratio δhmax/He lies between 0.02% and
0.03% although the data seems to follow more closely the 0.02% trend line.
High ratios of
0.035% are seen during Stage 8 and 10, attributed to the large unsupported distance between
struts.

EI=2025MPa;
• Es: stiﬀness of the soil layer at which the maximum deﬂection occur - Eur from Table
4.4.4;
• Eseq: equivalent soil stiﬀness as per deﬁned in Chapter 3, Section 3.3.
Eseq= 496MPa;
• havg: weighted average spacing between supports at any given stage.
The lower values correspond to NUP-IN22 and the higher to NUP-IN23. The height system
stiﬀness are attributed to the shallow excavations (small havg).
There is a large scatter in the data and it seems that movement is independent of the system
stiﬀness. A possible explanation for the lack of dependency on system stiﬀness is that once
suﬃcient stiﬀness is available, movement is determined by the magnitude of excavation base
heave. Moreover, at Nuuks Plads, the UCL layer is encounter at a relatively shallow depth
(≃14m) and this stiﬀsoil has signiﬁcant capacity to self-support (Long, 2001).
Figure 4.4.19: Relative Stiﬀness compared to normalized displacements
Figure 4.4.20: Relative Equivalent Stiﬀness compared to normalized displacements
Page 113
==PAGE:140==
Chapter 4. Stations
4.4.7
Summary and Conclusions
The stratigraphy at the site is homogeneous with a layer of clay till overlying meltwater sand/-
gravel. The 22.5m deep excavation is supported by means of 27m long secant pile walls and 3
levels of struts. The results can be summarized as follows:
• The UCL I layer is encountered a depth of z=-14.8m;
• δhmax varies between 5.5-6.1mm at the end of the excavation stages;
• δhmax occur withing the UCL I layer at 0.7Hex;
• δhmax/Hex varies between 0.02-0.035%.
It was found that there is not a signiﬁcant variation of displacement due to the relative system
stiﬀness. NUP-IN21 and 23 presented similar deﬂected shape and magnitude in displacement.
A reason for this may be their proximity to the transversal secant pile, while NUP-INN22 is
located at the center of the main excavation. However, because they are close to each other,
similar behaviour was expected for all of them. Previous study of Nuuks Plads presented by
Vranau (2016) mentioned that it was expected that NUP-IN22 would be located in a zone of
large openings in the slab, but this was not the case and that the behaviour of this inclinometer
may be attributed mostly to the fact that it is located in the center of the longitudinal wall.
Page 114
==PAGE:141==
Chapter 4. Stations
4.5
Nørrebros Runddel
Nørrebros Runddel station (NOR) is located in the area that today is part of Assistens Kirkeg˚ards
Afdeling G (Assistens Cementary) on the corner between Jagtvej and Nørrebrogade. There are
no buildings in the immediate proximity of the station, as shown in the plan view in Figure 4.5.1
(distance >20m).
Figure 4.5.1: Site view of Nørrebros Runddel Station, marked within blue lines (taken from Google
Earth).
4.5.1
Design Features
Nørrebros Runddel is considered a wide excavation, with a width of 18.6m between lining walls.
The station is supported by means of secant piles walls, installed with a length of up to 28m.
The excavation is carried out by means of a modiﬁed construction method with permanent
(top, intermediate and bottom) slabs and temporary steel struts (four levels). The main design
features are summarized as follows (all levels in mDVR90):
• Ground Level is at z≈+9.4m;
• Area of the station is approximately 11700m2 (63.2x18.5m2);
• Cut oﬀlevel for the retaining walls in level −20.39m;
• Excavation level within the station at z≈-14.4m.
4.5.2
Geotechnical Conditions
The results of the soil investigation carried out in the area are presented by the designer in
the ‘Nørrebros Runddel - Geotechnical Interpretative Report’ (Metroselskabet, 2012q). The site
stratigraphy characteristics is summarized as follows:
• Fill thickness vary from 1 to 3m.
• A 0-6m thick layer of upper clay till is located below the ﬁll layer.
• A 10-13m thick layers of meltwater sand and gravel overlays the limestone.
• The glacially disturbed zone of the limestone is approximately 1.3m thick.
• The transition from UCL to MCL occurs at the level of z=-23m, approximately.
Page 115
==PAGE:142==
Chapter 4. Stations
• Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders.
The borehole plan for site investigation is presented in Figure 4.5.2. Based on this, the ground
conditions at the construction site are proposed in Table 4.5.1 and the stratigraphy is shown in
Figure 4.5.3. For the identiﬁcation of the individual layers, geological description, classiﬁcation
tests and results of laboratory and geotechnical/geophysical in situ tests were employed.
Figure 4.5.2: Borehole plan at Nørrebros Runddel Station (Metroselskabet, 2012p).
Table 4.5.1: Soil and limestone at Nørrebros Runddel (Metroselskabet, 2012p).
Page 116
==PAGE:143==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.5.3: Layering of soil and limestone at Nørrebros Runddel (Metroselskabet, 2012p).
The stratigraphy is largely dominated by the meltwater sand. The highly permeable Upper
Copenhagen Limestone (UCL(HP)) starts approximately at a depth of z=-7.5m. Overlying the
UCL(HP), relatively homogeneous soil layers of ﬁll (FY), upper clay till (ML1), middle melt-
water sand and gravel (DS2/DG2) are found. The detailed geological description encountered
is summarized in Appendix F.1.
4.5.2.1
Design Proﬁles
The lower and upper bound characteristic parameters are selected as estimates of the values
aﬀecting the occurrence of the relevant limit state. The designer states that these shall be used
as most unfavourable for the occurrence of the limit state being considered.
Based on the relatively consistent homogeneous soil proﬁle encountered in borings C1205,
C1206, C1208, C1211 and C1218, proﬁles have been proposed in the ‘GIR Level III’ and shown
in Table 4.5.2. These proﬁles represent the lower bound proﬁles, being the most critical when
using the lower bound parameters. Following preliminary design input, which yield no signif-
icant diﬀerence in displacement or moment distribution, the proﬁle chosen by the designer is
shown in Table 4.5.3 and its geotechnical design parameters are summarized in Table 4.5.4. A
justiﬁcation in the choice of geotechnical parameters is presented in Appendix F.2.
The results of additional soil investigation along with sensitivity analyses performed conﬁrm
the validity of assumption made for selection of design parameters. The design of the retain-
ing wall based on these geotechnical design parameters is conservative enough to assure a safe
working place and stability of structures as well for the surrounding buildings (Metroselska-
bet, 2012p).

==PAGE:144==

4.5.2.2
Water Levels
The design water levels are deﬁned in accordance to the GIR III. The groundwater levels used
in the design of the station are presented in Table 4.5.5. The primary water table is considered
for the SLS and ULS analyses for the secondary water table is in close proximity. For the ALS
Page 118
==PAGE:145==
Chapter 4. Stations
analysis, the piezometric head in the primary and secondary aquifer is considered to ensure a
safe working place and the stability of structures.
The assumptions of water levels are conservative, since the return period for the temporary
structure is limited to maximum about 2 years lifespan and the primary aquifer is considered at
maximum level. Furthermore, mitigation measures are to be put in action during construction
stages. Both the primary and secondary water levels are considered for the permanent state.
Table 4.5.5: Groundwater levels at Nørrebros Runddel station (Metroselskabet, 2012p).
4.5.3
Retaining System Characteristics
Nørrebros Runddel has a maximum excavation depth of 24.06m.
The retaining systems is
a secant pile wall, with the piles properly overlapped to a depth of 28m (pile head level at
+7.61m, toe level at -20.39m, embedment depth of 5.83m) in the main box and 12.5m in the
main entrance area. The piles are 1m in diameter and spaced at 800mm.
4.5.3.1
Permanent Structures
Nørrebros Runddel’s permanent structures include the retaining wall, a single-line secant piles
wall, extending up to a depth of 28m and a series of permanent slabs, cast after completion.

The properties of the secant piles are summarized below in Table 4.5.6 and are based on the
‘General Retaining Wall Calculation Report’ (Metroselskabet, 2012d). A plan view of the station
illustrating the pile walls is shown in Figure 4.5.4.

Permanent Slabs
The retaining wall is supported in its permanent state by the interior structures, which includes
slabs at diﬀerent levels of the station. The thickness of the slabs are summarized below:
• Roof Level: Varies with an equivalent area of Aeq = 0.73m2/m;
• Concourse Level: 0.62m;
• Technical Level: 0.40m;
• Intermediate Level: 1.8m;
• Platform Level: 0.25m;
• Below Platform Level:Varies.
In the permanent stage, only the roof slab will be connected to the retaining walls and is
allowed to act in tension/compression.
4.5.3.2
Temporary Support Systems
The temporary steel struts are designed to prevent any excessive settlement during construction
and are kept in compression by means of hydraulic jacks during the construction phase.
Four rows of struts are installed during the excavation phases. The ﬁrst row of struts is in-
stalled directly on to the capping beam, while the 3 remaining rows of struts are interconnected
through horizontal steel beams consisting of double HEB.
The top slab is partially installed at the center of the excavation, as seen in Figure 4.5.6 and
the ﬁrst level of struts is located close to that of the top slab (z=+5.91m), below the top slab
there are three level of struts. The plan view and cross section illustrating the station layout
are presented in Figures 4.5.5 through 4.5.8. The steel tubes used during construction have the
following characteristics:
• Geometry

2nd, 3rd, 4th Level - Ø813x25mm
Emergency Exit - Ø419x10mm
• Spacing
1st Level - 5.5m

Emergency Exit - 5.0m

4.5.4
Construction Sequence
The executive phases of construction of the main box of Nørrebros Runddel were presented in
‘General RW Calculation Report’(Metroselskabet, 2012d) and are summarized below:
• Stage 1
Excavation to working level to z = +7.61m and construction of guidewalls and shallow
secant walls.
• Stage 2
Construction of deep secant walls.
• Stage 3
Main excavation to level z = +4.66m followed by the construction of the roof level slab
(between axis ‘C’ and ‘J’) at z = +7.72m, as seen in Figure 4.5.6 and the installation of
the ﬁrst level of steel struts to level z = +5.92m.
• Stage 4
Excavation to level z = −1.66m followed by the installation of the second level of struts
at z = −0.19m.
• Stage 5
Excavation to level z = −4.56m followed by installation of the third temporary bracing
level z = −2.71m.
• Stage 6
Excavation to z = −11.48m followed by installation of the fourth level of steel struts at
Page 123
==PAGE:150==
Chapter 4. Stations
z = −9.63m.
• Stage 7
Final excavation to z = −14.91m for realization of the bottom slab.
• Stage 8
Preparation of the surface, positioning of waterproof membrane on the external face of
base slap and casting of foundation slab at z = −12.53m.
• Stage 9
Removal of fourth bracing level.
• Stage 10
Removal of third bracing level and construction of intermediate level slab at z = −5.56m.
During construction, it is ensured that dewatering is maintain to keep the water level 1m
below excavation.

4.5.5
Monitoring and Instrumentation Overview
The construction of Nørrebros Runddel is monitored from the beginning of excavation for the
top slab, until a few months after the completion of the station. In general, this project focuses
on the monitoring data of the secant wall obtained from the in-place inclinometers, for the hori-
zontal deﬂections of the wall and the monitoring data from the temporary bracing system from
the strain gauges, which reveal information on the forces acting in the struts.
The monitoring plan layout is shown in Figure 4.5.9, identifying inclinometers as NOR-IN##
and the load cells as NOR-LC-##.
Figure 4.5.9: Monitoring Layout in Nørrebros Runddel.
Page 125
==PAGE:152==
Chapter 4. Stations
4.5.5.1
Inclinometers
The inclinometers are placed within the secant pile and extend up to a depth of 32.4m and are
ﬁxed at this location. Three inclinometers are located within the longitudinal walls and one on
each of the transversal walls of the station, as seen in Figure 4.5.9.
Only the inclinometers on the long side of the main box are interpreted, assuming a two-
dimensional plane strain behaviour, considering that the shorter sides are believed to be aﬀected
by the concrete arching eﬀect. However, due to an installation error NOR-IN21 and IN22 were
installed in the soil next to the wall, for this only NOR-IN23, 25, 26 and 27 are investigated.
The manual recordings for all inclinometers occur at 0.4m, 2.4m and then with 3m intervals.
The following summarizes the characteristics of each inclinometers:
• INC 21
Located 2m away from the secant pile wall. After preliminary analysis, the inclinometer
cumulative displacement showed that the inclinometer had been disturbed at the early
stages of construction, due to this, it is not possible to relay on its measurements.
• INC 22
Located 1.7m away from the wall. The preliminary analysis of the cumulative displacement
did not yield any random results, but the deﬂected shape recorded by the inclinometers are
not consistent with the others, refer to Appendix F.3.1. The inclinometer is not processed
further.
• INC 23
No data is available for Stages 1 through 3. Recordings start on March 3, 2013 during
Stage 4: Installation of ﬁrst level of struts. The inclinometer is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’ with
no signiﬁcant structures in its surrounding; it is located within the open section of the
excavation.
• INC 25
No data is available for Stages 1 through 3. Recordings start on March 3, 2013 during
Stage 4: Installation of ﬁrst level of struts. The inclinometer may be inﬂuenced by the
installation of the emergency exit piles, its recorded measurements shall be used cautiously
when compared to those of the ‘free-ﬁeld’ inclinometers; it is located within the open
section of the excavation.
• INC 26
No data is available for Stages 1 through 3. Recordings start on March 3, 2013 during
Stage 4: Installation of ﬁrst level of struts. The inclinometer is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’ with
no signiﬁcant structures in its surrounding; it is located within the top slab.
• INC 27
No data is available for Stages 1 through 3. Recordings start on March 3, 2013 during
Stage 4: Installation of ﬁrst level of struts. The inclinometer is considered ‘free-ﬁeld’ with
no signiﬁcant structures in its surrounding; it is located within the top slab.
Although no information regarding the ﬁrst three stages of the project are available, the
remaining data is reliable and provides valuable information. The inclinometer distance from
the temporary bracing is shown in Figure 4.5.10. NOR-IN26 is the closest to a strut, at 0.5m.

4.5.5.2
Strain Gauges
The CMT designers chose speciﬁc struts to be monitored which are believed appropriate to
understand the overall behaviour of the structure. The struts have the same characteristics
and similar level of action is expected in the central part of the station. The maximum and
minimum loaded struts are located in axis K and axis C, respectively. Furthermore, two struts
loaded at the most common values are also monitored (axis D and J). The central struts were
chosen for they have the same target values as per axis D. Hence, it can be more useful if a
strange behaviour is registered among the others monitored in C and K to have the adjacent
struts monitored as well. Moreover, all the diagonal struts are monitored to understand the
corner behaviour.
The strut loads are measured with three sets of strain gauges on each side of the selected
struts, as seen in Figure 4.5.11. Figure 4.5.12 shows the location of the monitored struts. In
the event the alert and alarm limits are reached, the corresponding procedures described in the
Emergency Action Plan will be followed.
Figure 4.5.11: Position of strain gauges on struts/cross section (Metroselskabet, 2012r).

Page 128
==PAGE:155==
Chapter 4. Stations
NOR-IN25 reveals a clear ‘jump’ during Stage 12, at which displacements usually remain
constant. Its proximity to the secant piles in the emergency exit might have inﬂuenced this
behaviour. The increase in displacement is similar to that seen in the installation of a strut and
the interaction between the two walls might have increased the stresses behind the wall.
4.5.6.1
Lateral Wall Deformations
The ‘free-ﬁeld’ inclinometers considered in this study are NOR-IN23 and NOR-IN27 and rep-
resent the lower and upper bound displacements. Technically, NOR-IN25 showed the largest
displacement, but this inclinometer is located next to the secant pile wall of the emergency exit,
and the interaction between these two walls may have an inﬂuence in its behaviour. NOR-IN27
is located within the top slab, allowing a comparison between the other stations, whereas the
wall at NOR-IN23 is unsupported at the pile head. The lateral wall movements recorded during
construction are presented in Figures 4.5.14 and 4.5.15. Additional lateral deformation proﬁles
are presented in Appendix F.3.1.
NOR-IN23 shows outward movements at the top of the wall; this cantilevered-like behaviour
is expected for a pile wall unsupported at the head. There is a distinct change in deformation
between Stage 7 and 8, corresponding to the excavation and installation of the third level of
struts. The increase in the excavation and the introduction of a strut with a pre-load might
have allowed the wall to deﬂect towards this location. Referring to Figure F.3.1 in Appendix
F, a clear outward movement is recorded at all elevations except at 8.4m. At early stages, the
maximum displacement of the wall is located at a depth of 8.4m but this shifts to a depth of
14.4m, as excavation progresses. All inclinometers recorded the maximum deﬂection at z=14.4m
(DS/DG).
At NOR-IN27, during Stage 4, the top of the wall has a slight outward movement which can
be attributed to the ﬁx connection with the top slab while the subsequent movement inwards
may have been induced by the installation of subsequent struts, which pressure causes the head
of the wall to move towards the excavation and the shrinking and creep of the concrete slab
as it gains strength. After Stage 4, the wall’s deformation is a clear example of the behaviour
corresponding to that of a wall supported by high stiﬀness struts (Ou, 2006). However, the
maximum lateral displacement is usually located at a depth of 14.4m, up to 10m above the
excavation depth, deviating from the expected behaviour of having the maximum displacement
at the excavation depth as presented by Ou (2006) and its work in Taipei. This deviation may
be attributed to the stiﬀer soils encountered in Copenhagen.
Page 129
==PAGE:156==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.5.14: Lateral wall movements at NOR-IN23. Dashed red lines represent the excavation depth,
black dashed lines, the struts and thick black line shows the location of the top slab.
Page 130
==PAGE:157==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.5.15: Lateral wall movements at NOR-IN27. Dashed red lines represent the excavation depth,
black dashed lines, the struts and thick black line shows the location of the top slab. Inclinometer 27 is
located within the top slab and there is only 3 levels of struts.
A comparison between the lateral movements of all inclinometers, excluding NOR-IN21 and
NOR-IN22, at the end of the excavation stages, Stage 12, is shown in Figure 4.5.16. Additional
stages can be found in Appendix F.3.2.
Through the stages, there is an evident outward movement recorded by NOR-IN23 at below
the depth z=-17m; this behaviour is also observed to a lesser extent in NOR-25 and 26. As ex-
cavation proceeds and struts are installed, the top of the wall moves outwards while there is an
evident inward movement towards the excavation depth, this may be explain by the occurrence
of soft material at the top and stiﬀer material at the bottom of the site. This deformed pattern
changes as the excavation proceeds, by the end of the excavation stages, the displacements below
the excavation and close to the toe are close to zero.
As mentioned before, NOR-IN23 recorded the smallest displacements. The secant wall de-
ﬂected the most at NOR-IN25, which is located closed to a secant wall built for the emergency
exit. The construction of the secant walls in the proximity of NOR-IN25 induced a change in
the stress state which lead to an excess deformation. As expected, NOR-IN26 and NOR-IN27
record similar displacements.
Page 131
==PAGE:158==
Chapter 4. Stations
Figure 4.5.16: End of Stage 12: Preparation of Concrete Level. Dashed red lines represent the excava-
tion depth, black dashed lines, the struts and thick black line shows the location of the top slab.
A summary on the maximum deﬂection for inclinometers NOR-IN23 and 27 are presented in
Table 4.5.8 and 4.5.9. There is no clear pattern on the incremental displacements at Nørrebros
Runddel, for either of the inclinometers presented. The cumulative displacement during the
installation of a strut are smaller than during excavation, which may leads to believe that the
pre-load is eﬀective and controls deformations, while excavating leads to the unbalance of forces.
However, NOR-IN27 experience the largest displacement during the installation of the fourth
level of struts; this was observed also in NOR-IN26 and 27. This behaviour can be attributed to
the fact that after all the struts are in place, the system gains strengths and the wall retreats.
