Results: Lateral Wall Deformations
The lateral wall deformation for the end of Stage 10 using the parameters in Table 6.2.4 is shown
in Figure 6.2.3 and additional ﬁgures can be found in Appendix I.2.2.
A signiﬁcant overestimation occurs at the upper layers. The deep outward movement at the
top of the piles is not capture by the model, similar to AMH. All inclinometers presented this
outward movement except for KK-INN22 which behaviour is relatively better described by the
model with large discrepancies in lateral movement. Drawing attention to the limestone, Emax
and the adjusted kr seem to properly describe the behaviour of the rock all through the MCL
and UCL II layers.

presented in Table 6.2.5. The forces modeled are signiﬁcantly smaller than those measured,
specially in the middle strut. Similar to previous analyses, this is attributed in part to the
missing external loads.

6.2.4
Conclusions
The sensitivity analysis for Østerport showed that the limestone layer presented stiﬀer charac-
teristic than assumed by the designer who had chosen conservative values for the limestone to
allow the design to consider the most pessimistic scenario for settlements and deﬂection.
The deep outward movement at the top of the wall may be attributed in part to relatively
soft upper soil layers and stiﬀsoils/rock at the lower part of the retaining wall as well for
the connection between the top slab and the wall which may produce a rotation at this point.
Furthermore, increasing the stiﬀness of UCL II and MCL and using the lower bound of υ = 0.26
allowed a better prediction of displacement and curvature of the retaining wall within these
layers.
6.3
Vibenshus Runddel
Vibenshus Runddel was chosen based on its layered soils, the fact that the limestone is located at
a deeper depths than the other two stations and having a long (36m) wall which is unreinforced
in the last 8m. The excavation is 18.8m deep and 19.5m wide.
6.3.1
Design Inputs
The design inputs are based on that provided in the ‘Vibenshus Runddel -Permanent Structures
- Secant Pile Walls Calculation Report’.
6.3.1.1
Structural Elements
The model requires inputs for the structural elements interacting in the model such as the wall,
struts and top slab.
Retaining Wall
The required characteristics of the retaining wall are as follows:
• E: 33GPa
• Iw: 0.0613m4/m
• EI: 2.02x106kNm2/m
• L: 36m
Top Slab
Taking the opening in the slab into account, the designer presents the parameters listed above
to allow the slab to be modeled as a beam element:
• E: 35GPa
• Aeq: 0.64m2/m
• Ieq: 0.191m4/m
• EA: 22.4106kN/m
Page 212
==PAGE:239==
Chapter 6. Numerical Model
• K: 1.15106kN/m/m
Struts
The characteristics of the struts are as follows:
• E: 210MPa
• Ieq: 0.0039 m4/m
• Aeq: 0.0091m2/m
• EA: 1.90106kN/m
• K: 97.5103kN/m/m
There is also a 550kN prestressing force applied to each strut after installation, the equivalent
prestress force is deﬁned as:
Feq = 550kN/spacing = 550kN/5.5m = 110kN/m
6.3.1.2
Groundwater conditions
The ground water level was taken in accordance to the design as the Primary GWL at the SLS
in Section 4.6.2.2 (at z=+4.8m or -6.2m). As the excavation progresses, the GWT is lowered
one meter below the excavation - this has been accounted for in the modeling.
6.3.1.3
Surface Loads
The load acting on the left side of the wall is taken as the backﬁlling between the average ground
level and the top of the pile (1.9m of backﬁll and γs = 20kN/m3 = 38kPa). The variable loads
were not included in the model including traﬃc loads and loads resting on the top of the slab
during construction. These are believed not to inﬂuence in the response of the structure.
6.3.1.4
Design Stratigraphy
The design stratigraphy used in the analysis and by the designer summarized in Section 4.6.2.1
is presented in Table 6.3.1. Figure 6.3.1 shows the Frew model for VHR.

6.3.4
Conclusions
The sensitivity analysis performed for VHR conﬁrmed that the limestone layer behaved stiﬀer
than assumed by the designer and that the overall system could be described by the Emax. The
rotation at the top slab is not shown in the model and it may be that the stiﬀness listed by
the designer does not include the rotational stiﬀness of the slab and that Frew is not able to
predict a rotation at this point which inﬂuences the bending moment distribution along the wall.
There is a possibility that the soils have apparent higher stiﬀness due to the geometry of the
station: Vibenshus Runddel is constructed with two technical rooms at each side that may have
inﬂuenced the overall stiﬀness of the supporting structures and without these, the deformation
of the main excavation might have been larger.
6.4
Summary and Final Remarks
The three stations analyzed with the pseudo-FEM software, Frew, presented distinct deﬂected
shapes throughout the construction process. AMH and KK subsoil is characterized by the pres-
ence of soft ground at shallow depth which contribute to the outward displacement of the top
of the wall.
The UCL layer at AMH and KK is encountered at similar depth and within the excavation.
However, the stiﬀness required to describe AMH is much larger and the diﬀerence also applied
to the kr parameter. It seems that the rock in AMH behaves stiﬀer than in KK. VHR in the
other hand, is described by stiﬀness closer to KK.
This exercise limited itself to investigate the eﬀect that the variation of the limestone stiﬀness
and the Poisson ratio may have in the behaviour of the wall. As mentioned before, several factors
can inﬂuence the behaviour of the wall and through this analysis only a few have been consider.
The main conclusion that can be drawn from these models is that the limestone parameters are
very conservative and they do not describe, in any of the stations, the true behaviour of the rock.
However, the stiﬀness of the limestone is just one parameter that may contribute to the design
deviations from the true performance. These may be also be inﬂuenced by other geotechnical
parameters and characteristics, such as the assumed preconsolidation pressure, OCR, K0 among
others.
Moreover, there are a number of features of real soil behaviour that are not included in the
model. The model does not take into account the softening or hardening of the soil. During
primary loading, the stress:strain relationship is better described by non-linearity, meaning that
the stiﬀness undergoes degradation as the deviatoric stresses increase. All of these may have a
signiﬁcant inﬂuence in the results of ﬁnite element models.
Page 218
==PAGE:245==
Chapter 7
Conclusions
The monitoring data of seven deep excavations of the new metro line in Copenhagen, Cityringen
was interpreted with the use of time elapse, lateral deformed shapes at the end of each stage
and the load development of the supporting struts. All seven stations had similar stratigra-
phy, support systems (i.e. secant pile wall and bracing), excavation geometry and construction
sequence. In most cases, the lateral wall movements deviated largely from those predicted by
the designer. This may be attributed in part to the highly conservative design values and the
method of assessment of these. The main issues treated in this investigation were:
• Identiﬁcation of the ‘free-ﬁeld’ inclinometer;
• Development of displacements with respect to the construction timeline at available levels;
• Maximum displacement with respect to excavation height;
• Inﬂuence of the stiﬀness of the soil in contact with the retaining wall and that being
excavated;
• Location and magnitude of the maximum displacement;
• Strut load development and correlation to wall displacement;
• Bending moment distribution considering a ‘ﬁxed’ and ‘free’ connection.
Based on the interpretation of monitoring data from the inclinometers of the seven stations
in the Cityringen and considering the ‘free-ﬁeld’ inclinometers, the following conclusions can be
made regarding the wall behaviour:
• There is an increasing movement with increasing relative system stiﬀness, ρ, as per deﬁned
in Section 3.3 which can be described with a logarithmic regression line;
• The relationships provide better approximations when using the re-deﬁned relative equiv-
alent stiﬀness, ρeq2;
• A normalized deﬂected shape describes the lateral deformation of a secant pile wall in the
Copenhagen subsoil;
• The location of the limestone seems to aﬀect the magnitude of the displacements;
• High soil equivalent stiﬀness leads to smaller deﬂections;
• Soft shallow ground allows the outward movement of the wall while having a deep inward
movement towards 0.6He;
• Hybrid bottom-up method mitigates the lateral wall deﬂections;
• The connection with the top slab prevents movements and leads to rotations.
• The largest moment occurs at the head of the wall when ‘ﬁxed’ and close to the ﬁnal
excavation depth when ‘free’.
Based on the interpretation of the monitoring data from the strain gauges, the following
conclusions can be made:
219
==PAGE:246==
Chapter 7. Conclusions
• Struts introduce a sharp increase in lateral load which results in a sudden increase of
inward displacement;
• The strut loads stabilize towards the completion of the excavation stages of the project,
as so the displacements;
• The location of the struts do not seem to aﬀect the inclinometers in any distinct way.
With respect to the numerical model, the following conclusions can be drawn:
• The limestone’s design operational elastic modulus has been deemed highly conservative;
• The soil for all sites shows a stiﬀer behaviour than that predicted by the designer;
• For future projects, re-assessment of the design parameters should be consider.
7.1
Future Work
The analyses in this thesis had limitations that can be in part cover by the following proposed
future work:
• 2D or 3D ﬁnite element modeling of all stations, considering non-linear soil constitutive
models such as soil hardening;
• Parametric study of all strength and stiﬀness parameters;
• Investigation of the eﬀect of strut stiﬀness and pre-load on the development of lateral wall
deﬂections;
• Study of long-term displacements considering the changes in eﬀective stress induced by
the TBMs or the removal of struts;
• 2D or 3D analysis of the deep excavation following the as-builts provided by the relevant
authority.

Appendix A
Enghave Plads
A.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ‘Enghave Plads
Geotechnical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
A.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit consists of sand, gravel as well as clay/sand mull. The unit may be very organic
at some places and it is possible that it contains building debris and boulders. The unit has
a thickness of 2-2.5m in the Eastern side and about 5m at the Western part of the site. The
boring’s symmetric nature indicate a similar thickness trend.
It has been noted by the designer that a new sewer pipe was installed along the outside of
the Southern and Western retaining walls. The bottom of the pipe is located 5m below the
ground and because of this 5m of ﬁll layer has been included in the design proﬁles.
A.1.2
The Upper Clay Till Unit (ML1)
Most borings of Enghave Plads encountered upper clay till. The ML1 layer has been replaced
by the ﬁll unit at C1703, P.17101 and P.17102, due to previous deep excavation works. The soil
is overall cohesive, medium plastic and generally silty though at locations C1722 and EHP.L01
a few samples are described as very sandy.
The thickness of the ML1 unit ranges between a 0 to 3m thickness. Moreover, at locations
C1722, C1723 and C1724 an approximately 0.5m thick layer of clayey to very clayey sand till is
encountered at the bottom of the ML1 layer. The sand till is considered by the designer as a
transitional soil between a cohesive and cohesionless soil and its behaviour cannot be described
by either type. This layer is included in the design proﬁles as either ML1 or a combined DS/MS
unit.
A.1.3
The Middle Meltwater Sand Unit (DS2)
The geological description of the DS2 unit is that of a ﬁne to medium, very clayey to silty sand
soil. The layer is found in most borings and has a thickness ranging from 0.5-2m. The meltwater
deposit is described as very sandy silt in boring C1725. This is included in the DS2 unit due to
its limited extend.
225
==PAGE:252==
Appendix A. Enghave Plads
A.1.4
The Lower Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML2/MS2)
The unit is geologically described as silty to very silty clay and is encountered in most borings
in the site, with a thickness of 1.5-2.5m. Despite its homogeneous nature, the following has been
noted:
• Thin interposed layers of sand till encountered at borings C1726, EHP.L03 and P17.100.
• Interpose silt til in boring C1703.
• Gravel till encountered at C1704-1.
• Described as sand till at C1723 and C1724.
The unit is considered a transitional soil, having a behaviour of a typical cohesive and cohe-
sionless soil.
A thin layer of meltwater sand (DS3) is found in boring C1705, overlying the limestone layer.
Due to its size and extent, this sand is included in the ML2/MS2 unit. Till deposits may contain
cobbles and boulders regardless of that stated on the borehole logs.
A.1.5
The Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD).The classiﬁcation
of the rock based on insitu observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times larger than those
obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture from rock cores is not
feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
A logstrategraphical is used to described the CL units. Lower CL and Bryzoan Limestone
are encountered in addition to the UCL and MCL. Flint bodies are also identiﬁed in the form
of subhorizontal layers ticker than 10cm. The core logs show that all degrees of induration are
present down through the rock formation, which is quite characteristic of the CL.High perme-
ability zone may occur at any random depth and a zone of increased permeability is point out
in the uppermost part of the limestone.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass involved
the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown Criteria
(Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass modulus
of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
The GSI for the limestone in Enghave Plads are summarized in Table A.1.1.
Table A.1.1: Estimated GSI from Enghave Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012i)

Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration and the strength
and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. The values in parentheses represent
the minimum and maximum values. The E-moduli are evaluated from the unload/reload curve
(Eur) from UCS tests.

A.2
Justiﬁcation of the selection of parameters
The following is a summary of that presented in the ‘Enghave Plads- Geotechnical Design
Report’.
A.2.1
Unit weight
The unit weight has been assessed as the average value for all the geological units. This assump-
tion is deemed adequate when incorporating the extensive soil and rock masses in relation to all
designs (STR/GEO, SLS and ASL and UPL). Furthermore, the slight variation in range has a
minor inﬂuence on the thrust acting in the retaining wall.
A.2.2
Angle of internal friction, eﬀective cohesion and undrained shear strength
The angle of internal friction has been assessed for plane strain design conditions as follows:
• φpl = 1.1φtriax for sand/gravel as the upper bound;
• φpl = φtriax for the lower bound: due to the transitional character of the sand till and the
content of silt and clay in the meltwater sand and gravel;
• φpl = φtriax for the clay and limestone.
Page 227
==PAGE:254==
Appendix A. Enghave Plads
The design values of friction angle have been selected conservatively in order to maximize
the thrust in the retaining wall and variation of this has minor inﬂuence on the uplift veriﬁcation.
The value of cohesion, c
′, has been set to zero for all soil layers, while it has been considered
for the limestone. Lower bound values have been investigated for the drained and undrained
parameters, which is a conservative assessment for evaluation of stress and deformation and
uplift veriﬁcation of retaining structures. Using a non-zero cohesion leads to reduction in the
design values for the wall/struts and in the deformations.
A.2.3
K0 and OCR Value
In the UCL and MCL layers the eﬀective vertical insitu stress, referred to the surface of the
glacial deposits, varies from a minimum values of σ
′
v0 ≊100 kPa acting at the upper bound of
UCL located at approx. z=-3.5 m, up to a maximum σ
′
v0 ≊280 kPa acting at the toe level of the
wall located at z=-20m. These values have been evaluated considering the eﬀective unit weight
of soils equal to 21 and 11 kN/m3 above and below z=+1.3m, respectively.
The average eﬀective vertical insitu stress of limestone layers at the depth of excavation at
a level z=-14.4m is equal to σv0 ≊220kPa. These values lead for an apparent overconsolidation
ratio OCR = σpc/σv0= 8.6 – 24, with σpc= 2400kPa. On the conservative side OCR = 10 has
been assessed and consequently, K0 = 0.43OCR0.6 = 1.71. The cohesion is assessed as a lower
bound value for UCL and MCL, the designer has chosen to use K0 = 0.78 for UCL and MCL
in the design of the retaining wall.
According to the “Annex to general design manual – Sensitivity analyses overview – Amend-
ment” for K0 values greater than 1.20 the inﬂuence of coeﬃcient of earth pressure at rest itself
on the retaining wall design is negligible since the lateral earth pressure is governing by the
coeﬃcient of active earth pressure. On the other hand, according to the ‘CIRIA report C580”,
during retaining walls installation “in situ lateral stresses are likely to reduce slightly’.
Hence, also considering that major value of K0 for limestone results not conservative for up-
lift veriﬁcation, when verifying uplift a lower bound should be used, equal to K0 = 0.36OCR0.33
= 0.78.
For the ML/MS, layers K0 has been considered an average value between the upper and
lower bound correlation, corresponding to K0=0.93 based on an OCR=10.
For the FY layers K0 = 0.577 has been assessed as conservative value based on OCR=1 and
taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.
A.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5.
The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions, while the ‘unload-reload’
value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.For FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case
the maximum value is already considered, based on designer experience, an operational modulus
Page 228
==PAGE:255==
Appendix A. Enghave Plads
and furthermore a conservative value for ﬁll deposits.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev. II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass = 800 −
1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geophysical
tests (G0 = 1200 −2000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3120 −5200MPa considering υ = 0.3,
divided afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value to be
used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.

Appendix B
Vibenshus Runddel
B.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Vibenshus Runddel
Geotechnical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
B.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit (FY) consists of slightly organic to very organic sand, clayey sand and sandy
clay as well as sandy gravel. The ﬁll and topsoil are combined into the FY unit, which has a
thickness ranging from 0.8m to 2.2m. The ﬁll deposits may contain building debris and boulders,
irrespective of what has been stated on the borehole logs.
B.1.2
The Upper Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML1/MS1)
The upper clay till and sand till unit is encountered in all borings. The upper clay till layer
is a medium plastic cohesive soil to a very sandy clay till. The thickness of the upper clay till
and sand till unit (ML1/MS1) ranges from 2.1m to 8.6m. The clay and sand till are considered
a transitional soil between a typical cohesive and cohesionless soil, hence neither characteristic
can be given.
B.1.3
The Middle Meltwater Sand and Gravel Units (DS2/DG2)
The meltwater sand/gravel units (DS2/DG2) ranges from ﬁne, sorted, very silty to medium-
coarse, very gravelly sand and gravel. The thickness of the meltwater sand and gravel varies
from 11m to 19m.
B.1.4
The Middle Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML2/MS2)
The middle clay till and sand till unit is found in all borings except in the Western part of the
site. The middle clay till layer varies from very sandy to very clayey sand till. Because of this,
the soil is regarded as a transitional soil between a cohesive soil and a typical cohesionless soil.
Design parameters are assessed for clay till (ML) and the frictional soil (MS) is described by the
DS/DG unit, due to their similar mechanical properties. The thickness of the soil layer ranges
from 0.5m to approximately 3.6m. In boring P01.101 the till unit is present as one or more large
granitic boulders between level −8.2m and −9.4m and were drilled through.
232
==PAGE:259==
Appendix B. Vibenshus Runddel
B.1.5
The Meltwater and Interstadial Clay Units (DL2)
The interstadial clay and meltwater layer is found across the station area.
It is a medium
to highly plastic clay with a minor organic content that does not inﬂuence the geomechanical
properties of the soil. The meltwater clay is described as medium plastic in boring C0920 and
silty clay in boring P09.100. In boring C0917, C0920 and P09.100 and the 0.5m to 1.5m thick
layers of meltwater clay and the interstadial clay thickness ranges from 1m to 5.3m in boring
P09.102 and C0907, respectively.
B.1.6
The Lower Meltwater Sand and Gravel Units (DS3/DG3)
The geological description of the lower meltwater sand/gravel units range from ﬁne-medium,
sorted to medium-coarse, poorly sorted over coarse, very gravelly to gravel. The layer has a
thickness of 1-7m, approximately. Gravel was found in some borings (C0910,C0904, P09.101
and C0907), above the limestone, having a thickness between 1m to 3.5m.
B.1.7
The Lower Clay Till Unit (ML3)
The lower clay till unit (ML3) is encountered in two borings within the project area. In boring
P09.100, the layer is 2m thick and described as a medium plastic clay to highly plastic clay till;
in boring C0920, the layer is 5m thick and very sandy clay till. Towards the top of the limestone
the till in C0920 becomes more sandy and is described as sand till. The very sandy clay till is
regarded as a transitional soil and their behaviour is either cohesive or cohesionless. The design
parameters are given for clay till (ML).
Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders, regardless of what has been stated on the
borehole logs.
B.1.8
The Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD). Due to the dis-
turbance of the drilling process, the geomechanic descriptions of the fractures on the rock core
is not representative. Referring to the General Interpretative Report (Metroselskabet, 2014g),
the in-situ observation classiﬁcation system yields RQD values 3-5 times larger than the ones
obtained through core logging.
The degree of induration ranges from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly indurated (H5). The
general character of the Copenhagen Limestone is that all degrees of induration are present down
through the formation. From the available borings and borehole logs, certain zones of increased
permeability within the upper part of the UCL unit were identiﬁed. It is also concluded that
this layer cannot be distinguished from the rest of the UCL, based on the typical induration or
densities.
The rock mass properties are derived from the Geological Strength Index (GSI) on the basis
of Marinos et al. (2007). The GSI is used to upscale the lab test results on rock matrix to the
properties of the rock mass.
The index is based on an assessment of the lithology, structure and condition of discontinuity
surfaces in the rock mass. It is estimated from visual examination of the rock mass exposed
in outcrops and borehole cores. Once the GSI has been established, it is entered into a series
Page 233
==PAGE:260==
Appendix B. Vibenshus Runddel
of empirical equations to estimate rock mass properties, such as the rock mass modulus of
deformation , as well for the compression strength, which can then be used as input into some
form of numerical analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
The GSI for the
limestone in Vibenshus Runddel are summarized in Table B.1.1.
Table B.1.1: Estimated GSI from Vibenshus Runddel (Metroselskabet, 2014f)
Table B.1.2 summarizes the trend values derived from speciﬁc test results for Vibenshus
Runddel, Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration
and the strength and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. The values in
parentheses represent the minimum and maximum values. The E-moduli are evaluated from the
unload/reload curve (Eur) from UCS tests.
Table B.1.2: Unconﬁned Compressive Strength, σc, Tensile Strength, σt and E-moduli of the Copen-
hagen Limestone in Vibenshus Runddel. (Metroselskabet, 2014f)

• φpl = 1.1φtriax for sand/gravel as the upper bound;

• φpl = φtriax for the clay and limestone.
The design values of friction angle have been selected conservatively in order to maximize
the thrust in the retaining wall and variation of this has minor inﬂuence on the uplift veriﬁcation.
The value of cohesion, c
′, has been set to zero for all soil layers, while it has been considered
for the limestone. Lower bound values have been investigated for the drained and undrained

uplift veriﬁcation of retaining structures. Using a non-zero cohesion leads to reduction in the

B.2.3
K0 and OCR Value
In the UCL and MCL layers the eﬀective vertical insitu stress, referred to the surface of the
glacial deposits, varies from a minimum values of σv0 ≊352 kPa acting at the upper bound
of UCL located at approx.
elevation z=-17.0m, up to a maximum σv0 ≊430 kPa acting at
UCL/MCL boundary at elevtion z=-24.0m. These values have been evaluated considering the
eﬀective unit weight of soils equal to 21 and 11 kN/m3 above and below elevation z=+4.5m,
respectively. The values lead for an apparent overconsolidation ratio OCR = σpc/σv0=6-7 for
the UCL and OCR< 6 for the MCL. On the conservative side, OCR=7 has been assessed for
UCL and OCR=6 for the MCL layers, giving K0 = 0.43OCR0.6 = 1.38 for UCL(HP) and 1.26
for UCL and MCL – Upper bound (According to GIR III).
According to the “Annex to general design manual – Sensitivity analyses overview – Amend-
ment” for K0 values greater than 1.20 the inﬂuence of coeﬃcient of earth pressure at rest itself
on the retaining wall design is negligible since the lateral earth pressure is governing by the
coeﬃcient of active earth pressure. On the other hand, according to the “CIRIA report C580”,
during retaining walls installation “in situ lateral stresses are likely to reduce slightly”.
Hence, also considering that major value of K0 for limestone results not conservative for up-
lift veriﬁcation, when verifying uplift a lower bound should be used, equal to K0 = 0.36OCR0.33
= 0.68 for UCL and 0.65 for MCL.
For the heavily overconsolidated glacial soils below elevation z=+9.0m the OCR>10 down to
elevation z=-6.0m. At the depth of excavation OCR=10, and below this level being reduced to
OCR=7 at the toe level of the RW located at elevation -z=15.5m. For these layers the designer
has chosen to use an OCR=10 above z=+9.0 and 8 below z=+9.0 for the ML/MS layers and
OCR=7 for DL layers.
For the ML/MS layers, the designer has used K0 = 0.43OCR0.33 corresponding to a K0=0.93
above z=+9.0m and 0.85 below.
For the DL layers, the designer chose K0 = 0.5OCR0.5 as an upper value.
For the FY layers K0 = 0.577 has been assessed as conservative value based on OCR=1 and
taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.

==PAGE:262==
Appendix B. Vibenshus Runddel
B.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5. The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions,
while the ‘unload-reload’ value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.
The Emax values are estimated by the designer based on the information given in the GIR
III-PD. The values are somewhat higher than the lower bound values for ML below +5.0. To
cover that a sensitivity analysis was carried out - minor values of operational Young moduli lead
to a slightly variation of internal actions and deformation of retaining walls.
For FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case the maximum value is already considered,
based on designer experience, an operational modulus and furthermore a conservative value for
ﬁll deposits.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −2000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3120 −5200MPa considering
υ = 0.3, divided afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value
to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.

Appendix C
Frederiksberg Station
C.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Frederiksberg Geotech-
nical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
C.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit consists of sand, gravel as well for peat/clay mull. The unit has an average thick-
ness of 1.0-2.0m. Yet, at boreholes C1517 and P15.101 a ﬁll layer with 4.0m thickness was
encountered.
C.1.2
The Upper Clay Till Unit (ML1)
The upper clay till unit was encountered at all boreholes below the ﬁll layer, with a thickness
varying from 5.0-9.0m and it can be described as a cohesive soil.
A 0.5m thick layer of very clayey sand till was located at C1513 and due to its limited extent
and thickness, the layer is incorporated in the ML1 unit. The boring also revealed an approx-
imately 0.5m thick layer of highly plastic meltwater clay and it has also been incorporated to
the ML1 unit.
Silty sand till (1m thick) was found in boring P15.102 at the bottom of the ML1 unit.
The sand is considered a transitional soil between the cohesive soil (ML1) and cohesionless soil
(DS/DG/MS), its behaviour is then attributed to both cohesive and cohesionless soil. The soil
is included in both the ML1 and the combined DS/DG/MS unit.
C.1.3
The Upper Meltwater Sand and Gravel Unit (DS2/DG2)
The geological description of the upper meltwater sand/gravel unit can be described as varying
from ﬁne, very silty sand to coarse sand and gravel. The thickness of the unit varies between
0.3m to 2.1m. The thin layer has been encountered in most borings.
The soil in P15.101 and P15.103 show that it can be described as gravel till but based on the
frictional characteristics of the layer it has been regarded as part of the combined DS/DG/MS
unit.
240
==PAGE:267==
Appendix C. Frederiksberg Station
Sand and gravel till deposits containing cobbles and boulders may be encountered irrespective
of the information provided by the borehole logs.
C.1.4
The Lower Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML2/MS2)
The lower clay till and sand till unit is a silty clay till with very thin interpose layers of sand til
at borehole P15.100. The sand till is located at the top of the clay till in boring P15.101 and at
the bottom for borings C1513, P15.101, P15.103.
In till deposits, cobbles and boulders may be encountered irrespective of the information
provided by the borehole logs.
C.1.5
The Lower Meltwater Sand and Gravel Unit (DS3/DG3)
The lower meltwater sand and gravel unit varies from silty, ﬁne to medium sand to coarse sand
and gravel. The unit has a thickness of 0.6m to 3.6m As seen in Figure 4.2.5, the unit was
encountered in all boreholes.
C.1.6
The Lower Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD). The classiﬁcation
of the rock based on in situ observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times larger than those
obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture from rock cores is not
feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
A logstrategraphical is used to described the CL units. Lower CL and Bryzoan Limestone
are encountered in addition to the UCL and MCL. Flint bodies are also identiﬁed in the form
of subhorizontal layers ticker than 10cm. The core logs show that all degrees of induration are
present down through the rock formation, which is quite characteristic of the CL.
The degree of induration of the limestone varies from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly in-
durated (H5). High permeability zone may occur at any random depth and a zone of increased
permeability is point out in the uppermost part of the limestone.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass in-
volved the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
However, this method is not applicable for soft rock and must be used with caution for H2
Limestone. The GSI for the limestone in Frederiksberg are summarized in Table C.1.1.
Table C.1.1: Estimated GSI from Frederiksberg (Metroselskabet, 2012l).
The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown Criteria
(Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass modulus
of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
Page 241
==PAGE:268==
Appendix C. Frederiksberg Station
Table C.1.2 summarizes the trend values derived from speciﬁc test results for Frederiksberg,
Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration and the strength
and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. The values in parentheses represent
the minimum and maximum values. The E-moduli are evaluated from the unload/reload curve
(Eur) from UCS tests.
Table C.1.2: Unconﬁned Compressive Strength, σc, Tensile Strength, σt and E-moduli of the Copen-
hagen Limestone in Frederiksberg (Metroselskabet, 2012m).
C.2
Justiﬁcation of the selection of parameters
The following is a summary of that presented in the ‘Frederiksberg - Geotechnical Design Re-
port’.
C.2.1
Unit weight
The unit weight has been assessed as the average value for all the geological units. This assump-
tion is deemed adequate when incorporating the extensive soil and rock masses in relation to all
designs (STR/GEO, SLS and ASL and UPL). Furthermore, the slight variation in range has a
minor inﬂuence on the thrust acting in the retaining wall.
C.2.2
Angle of internal friction, eﬀective cohesion and undrained shear strength
The angle of internal friction has been assessed for plane strain design conditions as follows:
• φpl = 1.1φtriax for sand/gravel as the upper bound;
• φpl = φtriax for the lower bound: due to the transitional character of the sand till and the
content of silt and clay in the meltwater sand and gravel;
• φpl = φtriax for the clay and limestone.
The design values of friction angle have been selected conservatively in order to maximize
the thrust in the retaining wall and variation of this has minor inﬂuence on the uplift veriﬁcation.
The value of cohesion, c
′, has been set to zero for all soil layers, while it has been considered
for the limestone. Lower bound values have been investigated for the drained and undrained
parameters, which is a conservative assessment for evaluation of stress and deformation and
uplift veriﬁcation of retaining structures. Using a non-zero cohesion leads to reduction in the
design values for the wall/struts and in the deformations.
C.2.3
K0 and OCR Value
In the UCL and MCL layers the eﬀective vertical insitu stress, referred to the surface of the
glacial deposits (z=+8.0m), varies from a minimum values of σv0 ≊245 kPa acting at the upper
Page 242
==PAGE:269==
Appendix C. Frederiksberg Station
bound of UCL located at approx. elevation -7.0m, up to a maximum σv0 ≊360 kPa acting at
the toe level of the wall located at z=-17.6m. These values have been evaluated considering
the eﬀective unit weight of soils equal to 21 and 11 kN/m3 above and below elevation 0.0m,
respectively.
The average eﬀective vertical insitu stress of limestone layers at the depth of excavation of
the shaft (z=-11.87m) is equal to σv0 ≊300kPa. These values lead for an apparent overconsoli-
dation ratio OCR = σpc/σv0= 7-10, being σpc= 2400 kPa. An OCR=9 has been selected as an
average value of UCL and an OCR=7 for the MCL layers. These values give K0 values of 1.61
and 1.38, respectively, applying the correlation for the upper bound: K0 = 0.43OCR0.60. As
the cohesion is the lower bound for the UCL and MCl, the designer has chosen to use K0=0.72
for UCL and 0.68 for the MCL to get a suitable conservative design.
The range of K0 of the limestone has been covered in a sensitivity analysis. According to the
“Annex to general design manual – Sensitivity analyses overview – Amendment” for K0 values
greater than 1.20 the inﬂuence of coeﬃcient of earth pressure at rest itself on the retaining wall
design is negligible since the lateral earth pressure is governing by the coeﬃcient of active earth
pressure. On the other hand, according to the ‘CIRIA report C580’, during retaining walls
installation “in situ lateral stresses are likely to reduce slightly”.
Hence, also considering that major value of K0 for limestone results not conservative for up-
lift veriﬁcation, when verifying uplift a lower bound should be used, equal to K0 = 0.36OCR0.33
= 0.78 shall be used.
For the ML layers, diﬀerent values of OCR have been taken into account according to GIR
Level III. For this reason an OCR value of 7 has been considered for ML above +4.0, while an
OCR = 10 has been applied below +4.0. In the design, the designer has used above +4.0 the
lower bound value K0 = 0.33OCR0.33 corresponding to a K0 = 0.62 and below +4.0 taken in the
interval K0 = 0.33OCR0.33 and K0 = 0.43OCR0.43 setting. This is due to the results presented
in the GIR III-PD.
For the DS/MS layers the OCR= 10. The K0 coeﬃcient used in the design is 1.12, which is
close to the upper bound assessed to K0 = 0.43OCR0.43 = 1.16.
For the FY layers K0 = 0.577 has been assessed as conservative value based on OCR=1 and
taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.
C.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5.The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions,
while the ‘unload-reload’ value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.
The Emax values are estimated by the designer based on the information given in the GIR
III-PD. The values are somewhat higher than the lower bound values for ML below +1.5. To
cover that a sensitivity analysis was carried out - minor values of operational Young moduli lead
to a slightly variation of internal actions and deformation of retaining walls. The results also
show that the maximum bending moment has slight variability around design value.
Page 243
==PAGE:270==
Appendix C. Frederiksberg Station
For the MS layer the E-value has been chosen close to the average value of the given span
(650-3900 MPa) based on very high SPT-values reported. Further sensitivity analysis for op-
erational Young modulus variation has been performed, focusing on the lower bound (between
1/3 and 1/10): these sensitivity analysis shows that when operative modulus of soils is varied,
slightly greater eﬀects on retaining wall can be appreciated. The results show that maximum
bending moment has a negligible variability around design value.
For FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case the maximum value is already considered,
based on designer experience, an operational modulus and furthermore a conservative value for
ﬁll deposits.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −2000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3000 −5000MPa considering
υ = 0.3, divided afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value
to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.

Appendix D
Aksel Møllers Have
D.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Aksel Møllers Have
Geotechnical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
D.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit FY consists of sand/clay mull, clay, sand and gravel partly with mull specks and
mull parts. The thickness of the unit ranges to about 2.5m. A symmetry is observed in all
borings. The ﬁll deposits may contain building debris and boulders.
D.1.2
The Upper and Lower Clay Till Unit (ML)
The upper clay till (ML1) unit is encountered everywhere on site directly below the ﬁll with
an average thickness of 5.2m with interpose layers of meltwater sand/silt and very locally sand
till. The soil may be described as clay till, very sandy, clay till, sandy, silty to clay till, medium
plastic, sandy, gravelly.
The sandy clay till refers to a clay of low to medium plasticity locally to a transitional soil
between a typical cohesive and cohesionless soil and its behaviour cannot be attributed to nei-
ther. Design parameters are assessed for both cases respectively (ML and DS), this also takes
under consideration the interposed layers of meltwater sand/silt into account.
Just below the upper clay till layer, in borings C1405 and C1406-2, a thin layer of high plas-
tic (sandy, silty) meltwater clay has been encountered but due to its limited extent (thickness
< 0.7m) it has been included in the ML1 layer. Moreover, at borehole P14.100, a 1m thick layer
of lower clay till (ML2) is located just on top of the limestone. The soil is described as clayey,
sandy silt till and it is included in the lower clay till unit.
Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders.
D.1.3
The Middle Meltwater Sand and Silt Unit (DS2/DSI2)
The dominant soil type among this unit ranges according to the geological description from ﬁne
very silty sand to medium, slightly gravelly sand with interposed layers of meltwater silt.
251
==PAGE:278==
Appendix D. Aksel Møllers Have
The thickness of the meltwater sand unit is approximately up to 8m. The silt layer have
been registered with a thickness up to approximately 2.5m. The geotechnical characteristics of
the (very) sandy silt are similar with the characteristics of the very silty sand, consequently,
they have been merged into the DS unit.
D.1.4
The Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD).
The classiﬁcation of the rock based on in situ observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times
larger than those obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture
from rock cores is not feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
A logstrategraphical is used to described the CL units. Lower CL and Bryzoan Limestone
are encountered in addition to the UCL and MCL. Flint bodies are also identiﬁed in the form
of subhorizontal layers thicker than 10cm. The core logs show that all degrees of induration are
present down through the rock formation, which is quite characteristic of the CL.
The degree of induration of the limestone varies from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly in-
durated (H5). High permeability zone may occur at any random depth and a zone of increased
permeability is point out in the uppermost part of the limestone.
The limit between UCL and MCL is based on the geological description of the core located
at approximately z=-15m and z=-18m.
However, as the limit level varies some meters and
geotechnical characteristic parameters are identical for the two units.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass in-
volved the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
However, this method is not applicable for soft rock and must be used with caution for H2
Limestone. The GSI for the limestone in Aksel Møllers Have are summarized in Table D.1.1.
Table D.1.1: Estimated GSI from Aksel Møllers Have (Metroselskabet, 2012f)
The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown Criteria
(Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass modulus
of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
Table D.1.2 summarizes the trend values derived from speciﬁc test results for Aksel Møllers
Have, Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration and
the strength and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. For one sample of H3

induration the compression strength and E-modulus are a little lower than the general trends

Modulus E

fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5.
The Emax values are estimated by the designer based on the information given in the GIR
III-PD. The values are somewhat higher than the lower bound values for ML below +5.0. To
cover that, a sensitivity analysis was carried out and minor values of operational Young moduli
lead to a slightly variation of internal actions and deformation of retaining walls.
For FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case the maximum value is already considered,
based on designer experience, an operational modulus and furthermore a conservative value for
ﬁll deposits.
The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions, while the ‘unload-reload’
value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −2000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3120 −5200MPa considering
υ = 0.3, divided afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value
to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.

Appendix E
Nuuks Plads Station
E.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Nuuks Plads Geotech-
nical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
E.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit FY consist of sandy clay, clayey sand, sand and sandy gravel as well as peat/-
clay/sand mull. The thickness of the layer ranges from 0-2.7m. The borings show a symmetrical
stratigraphy. The sand mull layer in boring P13.101 may be topsoil and not ﬁll but it is con-
sidered ﬁll unit as well for the peat mull in borehole P13.100 due to comparable mechanical
properties and limited thickness (< 0.5m).
The ﬁll deposits may contain building debris and boulders, irrespective of what has been
stated in the borehole logs.
E.1.2
The Upper Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML/MS)
The upper clay/sand till unit is found in all borings below the ﬁll unit. The upper clay till layer
refers to a cohesive soil of very sandy to very silty clay till with low to medium plasticity. The
thickness of the unit varies from 1.5m in boring C1803 to approximately 10m in boring P13.102.
The soil found in boring C1305-2 is identiﬁed as very silty and sandy clay till, the soil has
been regarded as a transitional soil between a typical cohesive soil and a typical cohesionless
soil, where their behaviour as to acting as either a cohesive or cohesionless soil cannot be given.
The design parameters are therefore assessed for both cases ML and MS.
From approximately level z=-1m, at borings P13.101 and P13.104, a thin layer of meltwater
sand is found interposed within the ML unit. Because the DS/DG unit is found around this
level at some borings (P13.101), both units have been included in the design proﬁles from level
z=-1m. Due to the transitional soil behaviour of the ML/MS unit a MS unit has been included
as a combined DS/DG/MS unit in the design proﬁle.
Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders, irrespective of what has been stated on the
borehole logs.
261
==PAGE:288==
Appendix E. Nuuks Plads Station
E.1.3
The Meltwater Sand and Gravel Units (DS/DG)
The meltwater sand/gravel units (DS2/DG2) are geological described as ranging from ﬁne, very
silty sand to medium-coarse sand and gravel. The thickness of the unit ranges between 1.5-6.5m.
A 3m thick layer of meltwater sand is interposed in the upper clay till layer and is considered
as a DS/DG/MS unit. A 0.5m tick layer of lower sand till (MS2) is found in boring C1318, on
top of the limestone, and due to its limited tichkness and extend the MS2 unit has been included
in the DS/DG unit. A very thin layer of sand till is located below the metlwater sand; based on
its limited extent and frictional characteristics, the layer has been included in the DS/DG unit.
E.1.4
The Upper and Lower Meltwater Silt Unit (DI)
In boring C1318 a very thin layer of very clayey silt are found below the upper clay till layer,
with a thickness of approximately 0.5m. Due to the minimal occurrence of the layer combined
with the layer’s characteristics being similar to the very silty clay till the silt has been included
in the ML/MS unit.
E.1.5
The Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD). The classiﬁcation
of the rock based on in situ observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times larger than those
obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture from rock cores is not
feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
A logstrategraphical is used to described the CL units. Lower CL and Bryzoan Limestone
are encountered in addition to the UCL and MCL. Flint bodies are also identiﬁed in the form
of subhorizontal layers ticker than 10cm. The core logs show that all degrees of induration are
present down through the rock formation, which is quite characteristic of the CL.
The degree of induration of the limestone varies from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly in-
durated (H5). High permeability zone may occur at any random depth and a zone of increased
permeability is point out in the uppermost part of the limestone.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass in-
volved the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
However, this method is not applicable for soft rock and must be used with caution for H2
Limestone.
The GSI for the limestone in Nuuks Plads are summarized in Table E.1.1.
Table E.1.1: Estimated GSI from Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012s).
The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown Criteria
(Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass modulus
of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
Page 262
==PAGE:289==
Appendix E. Nuuks Plads Station
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
Table E.1.2 summarizes the trend values derived from speciﬁc test results for Nuuks Plads,
Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration and the strength
and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. For one sample of H3 induration
the compression strength and E-modulus are a little lower than the general trends but still
within the test result from Cityringen. The values in parentheses represent the minimum and
maximum values. The E-moduli are evaluated from the unload/reload curve (Eur) from UCS
tests.
Table E.1.2: Unconﬁned Compressive Strength, σc, Tensile Strength, σt and E-moduli of the Copenhagen
Limestone in Nuuks Plads (Metroselskabet, 2012t).
E.2
Justiﬁcation of the selection of parameters
The following that presented in the ‘Nuuks Plads - Geotechnical Design Report’.
E.2.1
Unit weight
The unit weight has been assessed as the average value for all the geological units. This assump-
tion is deemed adequate when incorporating the extensive soil and rock masses in relation to all
designs (STR/GEO, SLS and ASL and UPL). Furthermore, the slight variation in range has a
minor inﬂuence on the thrust acting in the retaining wall.
E.2.2
Angle of internal friction, eﬀective cohesion and undrained shear strength
The angle of internal friction has been assessed for plane strain design conditions as follows:
• φpl = 1.1φtriax for sand/gravel as the upper bound;
• φpl = φtriax for the lower bound: due to the transitional character of the sand till and the
content of silt and clay in the meltwater sand and gravel;
• φpl = φtriax for the clay and limestone.
The design values of friction angle have been selected conservatively in order to maximize
the thrust in the retaining wall and variation of this has minor inﬂuence on the uplift veriﬁcation.
Page 263
==PAGE:290==
Appendix E. Nuuks Plads Station
The value of cohesion, c
′, has been set to zero for all soil layers, while it has been considered
for the limestone. Lower bound values have been investigated for the drained and undrained
parameters, which is a conservative assessment for evaluation of stress and deformation and
uplift veriﬁcation of retaining structures. Using a non-zero cohesion leads to reduction in the
design values for the wall/struts and in the deformations.
E.2.3
K0 and OCR Value
In the UCL and MCL layers the eﬀective vertical insitu stress, referred to the surface of the
glacial deposits at approx. z=+7.7m, varies from a minimum values of σ

v0 ≊192kPa acting at
the upper bound of UCL located at approx. elevation z=–6.5m, up to a maximum σv0 ≊340kPa
acting at the toe level of the wall located at z=-19.90m. These values have been evaluated con-
sidering the eﬀective unit weight of soils equal to 20 and11 kN/m3 above and below elevation
z=+3.8m. The values lead for an apparent overconsolidation ratio OCR = σpc/σ

for the UCL being σpc= 2400kPa. On the conservative side OCR = 8 has been assessed and
consequently, K0 = 0.36OCR0.33 = 0.72 for UCL. The correlation refers to Danish experience
form previous similar projects) and it is considered appropriate for retaining wall design.
For the heavily overconsolidated glacial soils below the elevation of z=+6.0m, the OCR> 10
down to elevation z=-9m. For these layers, according to the GIR III, the design values have
been assessed to K0 = 0.8 for DS/DG based on an OCR=10 and an average value between the
upper and lower bound correlation assessed from (Hanna et al., 2008) correlation:
K0 = (K0NC)OCRsinφ−0.18
Where K0 = 1 −sinφ.
For the moderately overconsolidated glacial soils (ML) above elevation z=+4.0m, values of

the clay till layer is not entirely continuous and it can be regarded as a transitional soil with the
underlying DS/DG layer.
For the FY layers K0 = 0.577 has been assessed as conservative value based on OCR=1 and
taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.
E.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/10 for the Quaternary soil layers and Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5 for
the limestone. This assumption is considered conservative and covers also very possible uncer-
tainties related to Poisson ratio of ML layers. Only in the ﬁll layer is Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/3,
because the resulting operational values are considered conservative for these kind of deposits.
The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions, while the ‘unload-reload’
value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −3000MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −3000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3120 −7800MPa considering

to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.

Appendix F
Nørrebros Runddel
F.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Nørrebros Runddel
Geotechnical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
F.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The ﬁll unit consists of sand, gravel as well for peat mull and clay mull. The unit may be very
organic at some places and it is possible that it contains building debris and boulders. The unit
has a thickness ranging up to 3m. The boring symmetric nature indicate a similar thickness
trend.
F.1.2
The Upper and Lower Clay Till Unit (ML)
The upper and lower clay till unit is a cohesive and low plastic soil. The unit has a thickness
range from 0 to 6m, with interposed layers of upper sand till and gravel till as well as meltwater
deposits consisting of clay, sand and gravel.
F.1.3
The Meltwater Sand/Gravel/Silt Units (DS/DG/DI2)
The geological description of the unit ranges between:
• SILT, clayey, very sandy
• SAND, ﬁne, very silty
• SAND, ﬁne, silty
• SAND, medium
• GRAVEL, slightly sandy, slightly clayey
The unit has a thickness between 10-13m. A 0.5m thick lower very sandy meltwater silt if
found above the limestone in boring C1206, possibly refers to a second layering in the lower part
of the sand formation. Furthermore, in situ tests identify the layer as dense to very dense, with
high SPT values, based on this the layer shall be considered as being highly overconsolidated.
F.1.4
The Copenhagen Limestone Units (UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD). The classiﬁcation
of the rock based on in situ observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times larger than those
269
==PAGE:296==
Appendix F. Nørrebros Runddel
obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture from rock cores is not
feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
Boring C1208 showed that the uppermost 1.3m of UCL is glacially disturbed. The strength
Compared to the intact limestone, the disturbed strength parameters are lower but it is consid-
ered to a moderate extent that this will not inﬂuence the design proﬁles. This one is not to be
mistaken with the high permeable zone (HP). The degree of induration of the limestone varies
from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly indurated (H5). High permeability zone may occur at any
random depth and a zone of increased permeability is point out in the uppermost part of the
limestone.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass in-
volved the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
However, this method is not applicable for soft rock and must be used with caution for H2
Limestone. The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown
Criteria (Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass mod-
ulus of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007). The average estimate GSI for Nørrebros
Runddel is proposed by the designer as 50.
Layers of ﬂint in the unit are usually 0.2-0.5m thick, but large ﬂint beds up to more than 2,
thick are present locally.
The results of the strength and deformation parameters for Nørrebros Runddel are inves-
tigated with respect to the other values present in the Cityringen as a whole. Based on this,
Table F.1.1 summarizes the trend values, with respect to:
• Speciﬁc test results from Nørrebros Runddel
• Tests from Cityringen
• Generally accepted relation between degree of induration and strength for the Copenhagen
Limestone (Frederiksen et al., 2002)
The E-moduli are evaluated from the unload/reload curve (Eur) from UCS tests.
It is
proposed by Metroselskabet (2012q) that the parameter design values be those of a combination
of the test results and the generally accepted trends.

since also this clay till layer is not entirely continuous and it can be regarded as a transitional
soil with the above DS/DG layer. Moreover, as per the above DS/DG layer, tests performed on
clay till specimens taken at Nør station show a behaviour close to the lower bound correlations.

taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.
F.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain.
For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal
to Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/10 for the layers in the upper part of the soil proﬁle and
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5 for the ML layer in the bottom part of the soil stratigraphy.
This assumption is considered conservative since it maximizes the thrust of the soil, in particu-
lar bending moment on excavation side and horizontal deformation. On the other hand higher
values of operational elastic modulus soil layers have been taken into account in sensitivity anal-
yses in order to catch the variation in negative bending (soil side) that can be found on the
upper and medium part of the retaining wall. The sensitivity analysis covers the possibility that
Page 272
==PAGE:299==
Appendix F. Nørrebros Runddel
higher stiﬀness is encountered in limestone.
The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions, while the ‘unload-reload’
value Eur is taken as 1.5 times the virgin one.
Only for FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case the maximum value is already considered,
based on designer experience, an operational modulus and furthermore a conservative value for
ﬁll deposits.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −3000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3120 −7800MPa considering
υ = 0.3, reduced afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value
to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
For design purposes, a lower value (Evc = 600MPa) has been selected in order to maximize
retaining wall deﬂection, bending moment acting on excavation side and axial loads on steel
struts. The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and
deformation of the retaining structure.

G.1
Detailed Geological Description
The geological description presented below are based on that presented in ´Østerport Geotech-
nical Interpretative Report GIR Level III’.
G.1.1
The Fill Unit (FY)
The unit consists of clay, sand and gravel with organic clay as well as clay and sand mull. Single
sample of organic postglacial peat and gyttja ﬁll appear in the lower section of the ﬁll unit. The
ﬁll unit has a thickness ranging from approximately 1.7m to 6m, however in the Eastern part
of the area the thickness is up to 8.5m (boring KKL03) and towards Northeast (KKL02) up to
10.5m. The symmetrix boring indicate similar thickness.
The ﬁll deposits contain building debris and boulders, irrespective of what had been stated
on the borehole logs.
G.1.2
The Lateglacial Unit (SS/SL)
This unit is encountered as 1m thick layer of medium plastic clay in borehole C0619 and as
2m thick of ﬁne to medium meltwater sand in borehole KK.L01. However, based on its limited
extend this unit is included in the FY unit for design purposes.
G.1.3
The Upper Clay Till and Sand Till Unit (ML1/MS1)
The upper clay/sand till unit is encountered below the FY or SS/SL units in all boring except
in the Northwestern part of the site at borehole C0614 and P06.102. The lack of till deposits in
this area might be due to the large amount of ﬁll encountered here (8 to 10.5m thick ﬁll).
The upper till can be geologically described as very clayey sand till and very sandy clay till.
This soil is considered transitional and neither characteristic of cohesive or cohesionless soil can
be attributed to it. Instead, design parameters are assessed for both cases ML and MS. The
thickness of the unit ranges from 0.3-4.5m, except for boring C0619 at which the thickness was
revealed of 5.9m
In boring C0605-2 a 0.5m thick layer of very clayey meltwater silt (DI1) is found below the
clay till and due to its limited extend it is included in the ML1 layer.
278
==PAGE:305==
Appendix G. Østerport
Till deposits may contain cobbles and boulders, irrespective of what has been stated on the
borehole logs.
G.1.4
The Meltwater Sand/Gravel Units (DS2/DG2 and DG3)
The meltwater sand/gravel unit ranges from ﬁne-medium, very silty to medium-course, very
gravelly sand and gravel; it is encountered throughout the entire site with a thickness ranging
from 2.6-9m. A 1m thick layer is located at levels z=-2/-3m in the eastern part of the site and
at level z=0/-1m in the West.
Moreover, a 0.5m thick layer of very silty, sandy meltwater clay (DL2) was encountered at
boring C0604. Because of the limited extent and thickness of the layer, it has been included in
the DS2/DG2 layer.
A 0.3-3.2m thick layer of meltwater gravel has been encountered on top of the greensand
deposits or limestone, as the deposits become coarser towards the bottom of the layer.
G.1.5
The Lower Clay Till Unit (ML2)
The lower clay till is encountered locally as a 0.4m thick layer in boring P06.101 and a 0.9m
thick layer in boring P06.102, at the top of the limestone. Because the nature of the deposit is
limited and only found locally, the unit is disregarded in the design proﬁles.
G.1.6
The Greensand Unit (PS/PK)
In the eastern part of the site the limestone is overlain by a 0.2 to 0.4m thick layer of Selandian
Greensand. The deposit is described as either clayey silty, sand (PS) at KK.L02 or grey to
greenish grey limestone (PK) at C0603-1. C0619 and P06.1010. Due to the limited extent and
thickness of the layer, the deposits are included in the DS2/DG2 unit. The greensand unit is
commonly forming a very dense conglomerate cemented together.
G.1.7
The Copenhagen Limestone units (UCL(HP), UCL and MCL)
The core description of the Limestone units involves the registration of degree of fracturing and
induration, as well for the core loss and the rock quality designation (RQD). The classiﬁcation
of the rock based on in situ observations have yield RQD values 3-5 times larger than those
obtained by core logging. Hence, the geomechanics description of fracture from rock cores is not
feasible, due to the high disturbance induced by the drilling process.
The degree of induration of the limestone varies from unlithiﬁed (H1) to very strongly in-
durated (H5). High permeability zones may occur at any random depth and a zone of increased
permeability is point out in the uppermost part of the limestone. Certain borings and boreholes
logs indicate zones of increased permeability in the upper part of the UCL unit.
The upscale of the lab tests results on rock matrix to the properties of the rock mass in-
volved the identiﬁcation of the Geological Strength Index (GSI) following Marinos et al. (2007).
However, this method is not applicable for soft rock and must be used with caution for H2
Limestone.
The GSI for the limestone in Østerport are summarized in Table G.1.1.
Page 279
==PAGE:306==
Appendix G. Østerport
Table G.1.1: Estimated GSI from Østerport (Metroselskabet, 2014c).
The GSI is entered into a series of empirical equations based on the Hoek-Brown Criteria
(Hoek et al., 2002), to obtain the rock mass properties. The properties, rock mass modulus
of deformation and compression strength, can be used as input into some form of numerical
analysis or closed-form solution (Marinos et al., 2007).
The surface dry saturated unit weight varies throughout the unit with relative regularity,
indicating a strength similarity of the UCL and MCL units. The variation of the density is
induced by and proportional to the variation of induration.
Table G.1.2 summarizes the trend values derived from speciﬁc test results for Østerport,
Cityringen as a whole and the common relation between the degree of induration and the
strength and deformation parameters for the Copenhagen Limestone. For one sample of H3
induration the compression strength and E-modulus are a little lower than the general trends
but still within the test result from Cityringen.
Table G.1.2: Unconﬁned Compressive Strength, σc, Tensile Strength, σt and E-moduli of the Copen-
hagen Limestone in Østerport (Metroselskabet, 2014d).
The Young’s modulus (E) from the UCS tests are evaluated from the unload/reload curve.
The designer proposes the lower and upper bound characteristic values presented in Table G.1.3.

==PAGE:307==
Appendix G. Østerport
Table G.1.3: Østerport characteristic parameters (Metroselskabet, 2014d).
G.2
Justiﬁcation of the selection of parameters
The following is extracted from that presented in the ‘Østerport - Geotechnical Design Report’.
G.2.1
Unit weight
The unit weight has been assessed as the average value for all the geological units. This assump-
tion is deemed adequate when incorporating the extensive soil and rock masses in relation to all
designs (STR/GEO, SLS and ASL and UPL). Furthermore, the slight variation in range has a
minor inﬂuence on the thrust acting in the retaining wall.
G.2.2
Angle of internal friction, eﬀective cohesion and undrained shear strength
The angle of internal friction has been assessed for plane strain design conditions as follows:
• φpl = 1.1φtriax for sand/gravel as the upper bound;
• φpl = φtriax for the lower bound: due to the transitional character of the sand till and the
content of silt and clay in the meltwater sand and gravel;
• φpl = φtriax for the clay and limestone.
The design values of friction angle have been selected conservatively in order to maximize
the thrust in the retaining wall and variation of this has minor inﬂuence on the uplift veriﬁcation.
The value of cohesion, c
′, has been set to zero for all soil layers, while it has been considered
for the limestone. Lower bound values have been investigated for the drained and undrained
parameters, which is a conservative assessment for evaluation of stress and deformation and
uplift veriﬁcation of retaining structures. Using a non-zero cohesion leads to reduction in the
design values for the wall/struts and in the deformations.
G.2.3
K0 and OCR Value
In the UCL and MCL layers the eﬀective vertical insitu stress, referred to the surface of the
glacial deposits at approx. z=+3.0m, varies from a minimum values of σ
′
v0 ≊140 kPa acting
at the upper bound of UCL located at approx. elevation z=-8m, up to a maximum σ
′
v0 ≊285
kPa acting at the toe level of the wall located at z=-21m. These values have been evaluated
considering the eﬀective unit weight of soils equal to 20 and 11kN/m3 above and below elevation
Page 281
==PAGE:308==
Appendix G. Østerport
z=+1.1m. The values lead for an apparent overconsolidation ratio OCR = σ
′
pc/σ
′
v0 in the range
OCR = 9-17 for the UCL and OCR ≤9 for the MCL, being σpc= 2400kPa.
On the conservative side OCR = 10 has been assessed and consequently, K0 = 0.43OCR0.6
= 1.71. The correlation refers to Danish experience form previous similar projects) and it is
considered appropriate for retaining wall design.
According to the “Annex to general design manual – Sensitivity analyses overview – Amend-
ment” for K0 values greater than 1.20 the inﬂuence of coeﬃcient of earth pressure at rest itself
on the retaining wall design is negligible since the lateral earth pressure is governing by the
coeﬃcient of active earth pressure. On the other hand, according to the “CIRIA report C580”,
during retaining walls installation “in situ lateral stresses are likely to reduce slightly”.
Hence, also considering that major value of K0 for limestone results not conservative for up-
lift veriﬁcation, when verifying uplift a lower bound should be used, equal to K0 = 0.36OCR0.33
= 0.78 for UCL(HP) as well for UCL and MCL.
For the ML layers the OCR values are set to OCR>10 as a conservative value. K0 has been
taken in the interval of 0.33OCR0.33 and 0.43OCR0.43, setting K0 =0.92 (OCR=10), assessed
as an average value, since the layers of clay/sand till and meltwater sand/gravel layers are non-
homogeneous and therefore might be regarded as transition zone.
For the MS and DS/DG layers, K0 has been taken as the upper bound value 0.43OCR0.43
setting K0=1.16 for an OCR value of 10.
For the FY layers K0 = 0.577 has been assessed as conservative value based on OCR=1 and
taking into account for the typical correlation of K0 = 1 −sinφ.
G.2.4
Modulus E
The operational elastic modulus used for the retaining wall analyses has been assessed as a
fraction of the elastic modulus at small strain. For soil layers, the stiﬀness ratio is equal to
Evc/Emax = G/Gmax = 1/5. The Young Modulus,Evc, is related to the ‘virgin-load’ conditions,
while the ‘unload-reload’ value Eur is taken as 1.6 times the virgin one.
The Emax values are estimated by the designer based on the information given in the GIR
III-PD. A sensitivity analysis for operational Young modulus have been performed in order
to explore a range of variation in the elastic modulus focusing on the lower bound (between
Emax = 1/3and1/10).
For FY layer, Emax = Evc because in this case the maximum value is already considered,
based on designer experience, an operational modulus and furthermore a conservative value for
ﬁll deposits.
The operational elastic modulus used for design of limestone layers has been derived from
Emass given in GIR Lev.
II. The Hook and Brown elastic modulus of rock mass Emass =
800 −1500MPa is close to small strain modulus determined from what measured in the geo-
physical tests (G0 = 1200 −2000MPa) and therefore Emax = 3000 −5000MPa considering
υ = 0.25, reduced afterwards by a factor between 3 and 4. It can be considered a reference value
Page 282
==PAGE:309==
Appendix G. Østerport
to be used in the retaining wall analysis.
The values mentioned are considered conservative for both determination of forces and de-
formation of the retaining structure.
